Sunnah of Sitting on the Minbar and Adhan Before Khutbah
Proof that sitting on minbar and adhan before khutbah are sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnah acts related to the Friday sermon and explain their proof from the practice of the Prophet (hadith).

Core Idea
Sitting on the minbar and calling the adhan before the khutbah are sunnah, not wajib.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah explains two sunnah acts of the Friday sermon: the imam sitting on the pulpit before beginning the sermon, and the adhan being called in front of him. The author clarifies the timing and provides a hadith as proof, though the hadith is incomplete in our text. These actions are recommended but not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sunnah acts
Read the passage and list the two actions described: sitting on the minbar before the sermon and calling the adhan in front of the khatib.
2
Understand the timing
The text says 'al-adhan bayna yadayhi ka al-iqamah' meaning the adhan is like the iqamah but before the khutbah. The iqamah is after the khutbah before the prayer. So the sequence is: adhan, khutbah, iqamah, prayer.
The author mentions 'two adhans and one iqamah' which may refer to a historical practice, but the standard Hanafi view is one adhan before the khutbah and one iqamah before the prayer.
3
Recognize the proof
The author cites a hadith from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid. The text is incomplete, but it indicates the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The hadith is zanni al-thubut (single transmission) and zanni al-dalalah, so it supports a sunnah ruling, not wajib.
4
Distinguish sunnah from wajib
In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah muakkadah means the Prophet consistently practiced it. Omitting it is disliked but does not invalidate the act. Wajib requires compensation if missed.
The passage explicitly says 'It is sunnah'.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may consider the adhan before the khutbah as wajib. The Hanafi school maintains it is sunnah based on the level of evidence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۷۹۴)[۳] خطبہ شروع کرنے سے پہلے ممبر پر بیٹھنا۔ [۴] خطیب کے سامنے اذان کہنا ، جیسے خطبہ کے بعد اقامت
ا
کہنا ۔ سنت ہے۔
تشریح : خطبہ شروع کرنے سے پہلے امام منبر پر بیٹھے یہ سنت ہے، اور اس وقت مؤذن خطیب کے سامنے اذان دے یہ بھی سنت ہے ۔ الاذان بین یدیہ کالا قامتہ : کہہ کر مصنف یہ سمجھانا چاہتے ہیں کہ ، پہلے خطیب کے سامنے اذان دے، اور بعد میں نماز شروع ہونے سے پہلے اقامت بھی کہے۔ اس طرح دواذان اور ایک اقامت ہو جائے گی۔
وجه : (۱) خطیب منبر پر بیٹھے اور اس کے سامنے اذان کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن السائب بن يزيد قال كان
Translation: (794) [3] Sitting on the minbar before beginning the sermon. [4] Saying the adhan in front of the khatib, like saying the iqamah after the sermon. It is sunnah. Explanation: It is sunnah for the imam to sit on the minbar before beginning the sermon, and at that time the mu'adhdhin should give the adhan in front of the khatib. By saying 'al-adhan bayna yadayhi ka al-iqamah', the author wants to explain that first the adhan is called in front of the khatib, and later before the prayer starts, the iqamah is also called. Thus there will be two adhans and one iqamah. Proof: (1) For the khatib sitting on the minbar and the adhan being called in front of him, there is this hadith: From al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid, he said: '...' [text incomplete].
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe that explains and proves two more sunnahs of the Friday sermon: the khatib sitting on the minbar before beginning the sermon, and the mu'adhdhin calling the adhan in front of him. The author clarifies that the phrase 'al-adhan bayna yadayhi ka al-iqamah' means that just as the iqamah is called before the prayer, the adhan is called before the sermon. This results in two adhans (one before the first sermon and one before the prayer?) Actually, the standard practice is one adhan before the first sermon and one iqamah before the prayer. The text says 'two adhans and one iqamah' — this might refer to the fact that historically there were two adhans for Jumu'ah, but the Hanafi practice is one adhan before the khutbah and one iqamah. The proof is a hadith from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid, but the text cuts off. The ruling is that these actions are sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms
منبر (minbar): The pulpit from which the Friday sermon is delivered.
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer; here it refers to the adhan said before the Friday sermon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on sitting on the minbar before the Friday sermon?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The imam sitting on the minbar and the adhan being called before the khutbah are sunnah acts, not obligatory, based on the Prophet's practice.

Sunnahs of the Friday Sermon
Enumerates sunnah acts of the Friday sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sunnah acts of the Friday khutbah and distinguish them from the pillars (arkan).

Core Idea
The Friday khutbah has multiple sunnah mu'akkadah acts; omitting them is disliked but does not invalidate the prayer.

The Friday sermon is a distinctive act of worship. While its essential pillars are necessary for validity, the Prophet's practice includes numerous recommended acts that perfect the khutbah. This passage enumerates those sunnah acts, each supported by authentic hadith, and clarifies their legal status as emphasized sunnahs rather than obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act described
Read the Arabic passage and identify each recommended action mentioned, from facing the congregation to listening attentively.
The list begins with 'istiqbal' (facing) and ends with the people listening.
2
Understand the basis in Sunnah
Each act is derived from the Prophet's practice as recorded in authentic hadith (e.g., Bukhari, Muslim). Note that the passage does not quote hadith explicitly but is built on transmitted practice.
The commentary confirms these are based on hadith.
3
Note the classification as sunnah mu'akkadah
In Hanafi fiqh, these acts are sunnah mu'akkadah — emphasized but not obligatory. Omitting them is makruh tanzihan but does not invalidate the Friday prayer.
This is in contrast to the pillars (arkan) which are fard.
4
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Some Shafi'i scholars consider certain of these acts as wajib. Understand the practical consequence: for Hanafis, missing them does not require repetition, while for Shafi'is it might.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the ruling
When studying or performing the khutbah, identify each sunnah and prioritize them, but do not mistake them for conditions of validity.
This prevents unnecessary invalidation of salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الخطبة واستقبال القوم بوجهه وبداء ته بحمد الله والثناء عليه بما هو اهله والشهادتان والصلوة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والعظة والتذكير وقراءة آية من القرآن وخطبتان والجلوس بين الخطبتين واعادة الحمد والثناء والصلوة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فى ابتداء الخطبة الثانية والدعاء فيها للمؤمنين والمؤمنات بالاستغفار لهم وان يسمع القوم الخطبة
The sunnahs of the khutbah: facing the people with his face, beginning with praise of Allah and eulogy upon Him as is befitting, the two testimonies of faith, sending blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, admonition and reminder, reciting a verse from the Qur'an, two sermons and sitting between them, repeating praise and blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ at the beginning of the second sermon, supplicating therein for believing men and women seeking forgiveness for them, and the people listening to the sermon.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage lists the sunnah (recommended) acts of the Friday khutbah. Each act is derived from the Prophet's practice as recorded in authentic hadith. The khutbah is a distinct act of worship, and while its pillars (arkan) are essential for validity, these sunnahs complete its perfection. The author first mentions facing the congregation, as the Prophet would turn to face them. Then starting with praise of Allah (hamd) and eulogy (thana'), which is the opening of many of the Prophet's sermons. The two shahadas (testimonies of faith) and sending salawat upon the Prophet are also sunnah. Admonition (wa'z) and reminder (tadhkir) form the core purpose of the sermon. Reciting a verse from the Qur'an is recommended. Two sermons are delivered with a brief sitting between them. In the second sermon, the imam repeats hamd and salawat, and then makes du'a for the believers, especially seeking forgiveness (istighfar). Finally, the congregation should listen attentively. These rulings are based on hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and others as cited in the Urdu commentary.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered before the Friday prayer or on two Eids, consisting of specified sunnah acts.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act established by the Prophet's practice; omission is not sinful but disliked.
استقبال (istiqbal): Facing the congregation directly during the khutbah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a sunnah of the Friday khutbah according to this passage?
A) Facing the people with one's face
B) Reciting a verse from the Qur'an
C) Raising the hands during supplication
D) Sending blessings upon the Prophet

Key Takeaway
The Friday khutbah is perfected by observing its sunnah acts, which are highly recommended but not obligatory.

Disliked Actions During the Friday Sermon
Ruling on disliked actions while listening to the khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four disliked actions during the Friday sermon and apply the ruling by identifying appropriate behavior.

Core Idea
Eating, drinking, playing, and turning away during the khutbah are makruh tanzih—leave them to earn reward.

This lesson addresses proper etiquette for the Friday sermon. While listening to the khutbah, certain actions are considered disrespectful. The Hanafi school rules them as makruh tanzih, meaning they are disliked but not sinful. Understanding this helps maintain the sanctity of Jumu'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text lists four actions: eating, drinking, playing (عبث), and turning away (التفات). The ruling is makruh (disliked).
Note the specific term 'عبث' includes any idle or distracting activity.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from Shuraih al-Qadi, a prominent tabi'i, reported in Musannaf Abdurrazzaq. It describes his behavior at the mosque on Friday.
Shuraih was a judge known for his piety; his actions are considered a strong practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Shuraih's practice of facing the imam and not looking around indicates that turning away is contrary to proper conduct. This is the basis for the dislike.
The athar does not explicitly forbid it, but the implied lesson is that one should not turn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may consider these actions haram or severely disliked, but Hanafis categorise them as makruh tanzih due to the lack of a definitive prohibition.
The difference arises from the interpretation of the command to listen attentively.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is makruh tanzih, as supported by early Hanafi sources and the athar.
One should avoid these actions to follow the sunnah, but the prayer remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنن الخطبة
(۸۰۶) وكره لحاضر الخطبة الاكل والشرب والعبث والالتفات۔ اور لوگوں کو خطبہ کے وقت کھانا اور پینا اور کھیلنا اور (منھ پھرا کر ) ادھر ادھر دیکھنا مکروہ ہے۔
وجه : عن شريح قال اذا كان يوم الجمعة اتى المسجد فان كان الامام لم يخرج صلى ركعتين و ان كان قد خرج لم يصل و احتبى و استقبل الامام و لم يلتفت يمينا و لا شمالا - مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل تحجي والامام يخطب ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۰ نمبر ۵۵۳۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ خطبہ کے وقت ادھر ادھر نہیں دیکھنا چاہئے۔
Sunnah of the Sermon. (806) It is disliked for the one present at the sermon to eat, drink, play, and turn away. Translation: And for the people, at the time of the sermon, eating, drinking, playing, and (turning the face) looking here and there is disliked. Proof: From Shuraih, he said: When it was Friday, he came to the mosque; if the imam had not yet come out, he prayed two rak'ahs; if he had already come out, he did not pray, and he sat hugging his knees, facing the imam, and did not look right or left. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab al-Rajul Yuhajji wal-Imam Yakhutb, vol. 3, p. 130, no. 5535). From this athar it is known that one should not look around at the time of the sermon.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a ruling on the conduct of the listener during the Friday sermon (khutbah). The text states that it is makruh (disliked) for the person present at the sermon to eat, drink, engage in idle play (عبث), or turn his face away (التفات) from the imam. The commentary explains that these actions are considered disrespectful. The proof provided is an athar (narration) from Shuraih al-Qadi, a prominent tabi'i, describing the proper etiquette: one should sit facing the imam, not turn right or left, and avoid even praying if the imam has already started. This is a dalil that shows the focus and attention required during the khutbah.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): In this text, makruh refers to an action that is disliked but not sinful; leaving it is better.
عبث (abath): Idle play or meaningless activity, such as fidgeting or playing with objects.
التفات (iltifat): Turning one's face away from the imam, looking around.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on eating during the Friday sermon according to this passage?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Mubah
D) Sunnah

Key Takeaway
Eating, drinking, playing, or turning away during the khutbah is makruh tanzih; avoid them to preserve the sanctity of Jumu'ah.

The Khatib's Greeting upon Ascending the Pulpit
Ruling on the khatib's greeting before the sermon

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the khatib's greeting when ascending the minbar, identify the proof from hadith, and explain why it is considered permissible but not a sunnah.

Core Idea
Greeting when ascending the minbar is permissible but not a sunnah; it is based on non-Sihah Sittah hadiths.

When the khatib ascends the pulpit for Friday khutbah, should he greet the congregation? The primary ruling states he should not. However, the commentary reveals a nuanced position: greeting is permissible based on prophetic practice, yet it is not established as a regular sunnah because the strongest hadith collections do not contain it. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the Hanafi reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the khatib greeting when ascending the minbar. The initial ruling stated is that he should not greet.
The ruling is presented as 'la yusallim' – should not greet.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is two hadiths from Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf Abdurrazzaq showing the Prophet greeted when ascending the minbar.
These are not from the Sihah Sittah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadiths indicate permissibility, but the Hanafi school relies on the absence of these narrations in the most authentic collections to downgrade the practice from sunnah to merely permissible.
The strength of the proof is evaluated by its presence in canonical books.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may consider greeting a sunnah based on these hadiths; Hanafis do not consider it established as a regular sunnah.
The difference stems from different criteria for sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is that it is mubah (permissible). The mufta bihi is that it is permissible but not a stressed practice.
The commentary states: 'if he does it, it is permissible'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۰۷) ولا يسلّم الخطيب على القوم اذا استوى على المنبر۔ ترجمه : اور خطیب قوم پر سلام نہ کرے جب وہ منبر پر آئے۔ تشریح : جب خطیب منبر پر آئے تو سلام کرنا کوئی سنت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ صحاح ستہ میں اس کا ذکر نہیں ہے لیکن اگر کر لے تو اس کی گنجائش ہے۔ وجه:(۱) عن جابر قال كان رسول الله الله اذا صعد المنبر سلم ۔ (سنن بیہقی ، باب الامام يسلم علی الناس اذ اصعد المنبر قبل ان مجلس ، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۸۹، نمبر ۵۷۴۱) (۲) عن عطاء ان النبي الا الله كان اذا سعد المنبر اقبل بوجهه على الناس فقال : السلام عليكم (مصنف عبد الرزاق ، باب تسلیم الامام از اصعد ، ج ثالث ص ۸۸ نمبر ۵۲۹۶ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب الامام اذا جلس على المنبر يسلم ، ج اول ص ۴۴۹، نمبر ۵۱۹۵) ان دونوں حدیثوں میں ہے کہ خطیب سلام کرے
(807) And the khatib should not greet the people when he ascends the pulpit. Translation: And the khatib should not greet the people when he comes onto the pulpit. Explanation: When the khatib comes onto the pulpit, greeting is not a sunnah, because it is not mentioned in the six authentic books (Sihah Sittah), but if he does, it is permissible. Proof: (1) From Jabir, he said: When the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ascended the pulpit, he greeted. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Imam Yusallim ala al-Nas idha as'ada al-Minbar qabla an yajlis, vol. 3, p. 289, no. 5741) (2) From Ata that the Prophet (peace be upon him) when he ascended the pulpit turned his face to the people and said: As-salamu alaykum. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab Taslim al-Imam idha as'ada, vol. 3, p. 88, no. 5296; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab al-Imam idha jalasa ala al-Minbar yusallim, vol. 1, p. 449, no. 5195). In these two hadiths, it is that the khatib greets.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a ruling on the khatib's (preacher's) conduct when he ascends the pulpit (minbar) for the Friday sermon. The initial ruling states that the khatib should not greet the congregation. The commentary explains that greeting is not established as a sunnah from the most authentic hadith collections (Sihah Sittah), so it is not a recommended practice. However, if the khatib does greet, it is permissible because there are narrations from Jabir and Ata that the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) himself would greet when ascending the pulpit. The presence of these ahadith shows that it is allowed, but since it is absent from the most rigorously authentic books, it is not considered a regular sunnah. The text thus presents a balanced view: the best is to not greet, but doing so is acceptable.

Key Terms
خطبہ (khutbah): The sermon delivered by the imam on Friday or Eid, which has specific rulings.
منبر (minbar): The elevated platform from which the khatib delivers the sermon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what is the ruling on the khatib greeting when ascending the minbar?
A) It is a confirmed sunnah
B) It is forbidden
C) It is permissible but not a sunnah
D) It is recommended and required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that greeting when ascending the minbar is permissible but not a sunnah, based on hadiths outside the Sihah Sittah.

Ruling on Leaving the City after the Jumu'ah Adhan
Ruling on leaving after adhan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the city after the Jumu'ah adhan and identify the proofs cited.

Core Idea
Leaving after the Jumu'ah adhan without praying is makruh tanzih due to disregard.

Jumu'ah is a weekly collective obligation. The adhan signals its time. Leaving the city after the adhan may indicate negligence. The Hanafi school rules this as makruh tanzih (lightly disliked), not haram, based on companion sayings and cautionary reports. This lesson examines the ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving the city (misr) after the adhan for Jumu'ah without having prayed. The Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzih.
The dislike is because it shows turning away (i'rad) from the obligation.
2
Understand the legal reason
The basis for the ruling is that leaving after the adhan reflects disregard for Jumu'ah. It may also lead to missing the prayer altogether.
This reason is derived from the concept of i'rad (neglect).
3
Examine the first proof
Mujahid reported that a group left when Jumu'ah was present and their tent caught fire spontaneously – a warning sign.
This is not a direct proof but a cautionary incident.
4
Examine the second proof
Aisha (رضي الله عنها) said: 'If you reach Friday night, do not leave until you pray Jumu'ah.' This is a stronger proof as a companion statement.
It implies leaving before Jumu'ah is discouraged.
5
Distinguish from haram
The ruling is makruh tanzih, not haram. If one returns in time and prays, no sin. Only if Jumu'ah is missed does the obligation need qada.
Some scholars consider it haram if it leads to missing; Hanafis see the act itself as merely disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۰۸) وكره الخروج من المصر بعد النداء مالم يصل۔ ترجمه : اور اذان ہونے کے بعد نماز پڑھنے تک شہر سے نکلنا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : جب جمعہ کا وقت ہو گیا تو اس وقت جمعہ پڑھے بغیر شہر سے نکلنا مکروہ ہے، کیونکہ اس میں جمعہ سے اعراض ہے۔ وجه : (۱) عن مجاهد قال خرج قوم و قد حضرت الجمعة فاضطرم عليهم خباؤهم نارا من غير نار يرونها. (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب من کره اذا حضرت الجمعۃ ان یخرج حتی یصلی ، ج اول ص ۱۴۴۴، نمبر ۵۱۱۹ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب السفر یوم الجمعة ، ج ثالث ، ص۱۳۴ نمبر ۵۵۵۳) (۲) عن عائشة قالت اذا ادركت ليلة الجمعة فلا تخرج حتى تصلى الجمعة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب من کره اذا حضرت الجمعة ان يخرج حتی یصلی ، ج اول ص ۴۴۴، نمبر ۵۱۱۴) اس قول صحابی میں تو یہاں تک ہے کہ رات سے ہی نہ نکلے۔ جب تک کہ جمعہ نہ پڑھ لے۔
(808) And it is disliked to leave the city (misr) after the call until he prays. Translation: And after the adhan, until the prayer is performed, leaving the city is disliked. Explanation: When the time of Jumu'ah has come, then leaving the city without praying Jumu'ah is disliked, because it is a turning away from Jumu'ah. Proof: (1) From Mujahid, he said: A people left while Jumu'ah was present, and their tent caught fire from no fire they saw. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab man kariha idha hadarat al-jumu'ah an yakhruja hatta yusalli, vol. 1, p. 1444, no. 5119; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab al-safar yawm al-jumu'a, vol. 3, p. 134, no. 5553) (2) From Aisha, she said: If you reach Friday night, do not leave until you pray Jumu'ah. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bab man kariha idha hadarat al-jumu'ah an yakhruja hatta yusalli, vol. 1, p. 444, no. 5114) This saying of the Companion goes so far as to not leave even from the night until one prays Jumu'ah.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This is a ruling about leaving the city (misr) after the call to prayer (adhan) for Friday Jumu'ah without praying. It is considered makruh (disliked) because it indicates disregard (i'rad) for the Jumu'ah obligation. The commentary clarifies that if the time of Jumu'ah has already entered, leaving without praying is disliked. The proofs include an unusual incident narrated by Mujahid where a group left during Jumu'ah time and their tent caught fire spontaneously—this is mentioned as a warning. A stronger proof is the saying of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) that one should not leave even from Friday night until one prays Jumu'ah, indicating great emphasis. The ruling applies to those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory, and the dislike is tanzih.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A large town or city where Jumu'ah is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaving the city after the adhan for Jumu'ah without praying?
A) Haram
B) Makruh tanzih
C) Mubah
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Leaving the city after the Jumu'ah adhan without praying is makruh tanzih, not haram, based on companion evidence and the concept of i'rad.

Those Not Obligated to Jumu'ah: Its Sufficiency for Zuhr
Ruling with proof from Tabi'i and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Jumu'ah suffices for Zuhr for those not originally obligated to Jumu'ah, and identify the evidence from Hasan al-Basri and the hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.

Core Idea
Jumu'ah, though not fard for some, fulfills the day's fard—one prayer suffices for the time's obligation.

This lesson addresses a practical point: what happens when a person who is not required to attend Jumu'ah, such as a woman or a traveler, chooses to pray it? The Hanafi school rules that their Jumu'ah is valid and replaces the obligatory Zuhr prayer. The reasoning is that every Muslim must pray either Zuhr or Jumu'ah on Friday, so performing Jumu'ah discharges that duty. The evidence includes statements from the Tabi'i Hasan al-Basri and a hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the individuals addressed
Determine who are those not obligated to Jumu'ah in Hanafi fiqh: women, travelers, the sick, and those legally excused from attendance.
The obligation of Jumu'ah (wajib) applies to free, adult, resident Muslim men.
2
State the ruling
If such a person performs the Jumu'ah prayer, it suffices for the obligatory prayer of the time (fard al-waqt), i.e., Zuhr.
The ruling is explicit: 'جاز عن فرض الوقت'.
3
Understand the reasoning (وجہ)
Although Jumu'ah is not personally obligatory for these individuals, they still have an obligation to pray either Zuhr or Jumu'ah on Friday. By choosing Jumu'ah, they fulfill that obligation.
This is a key logical point: one of the two is wajib.
4
Examine the first proof: Hasan al-Basri's saying
Hasan al-Basri stated that women who gather with the imam (for Jumu'ah) have it suffice for the imam's prayer (i.e., the fard). This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.
This is a qawl al-tabi'i, which is a proof in Hanafi methodology.
5
Examine the second proof: Hadith in Bayhaqi
Hasan al-Basri reported that women used to pray Jumu'ah with the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم). This shows that the Prophet accepted it, and it sufficed for their obligation. The hadith is in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
The hadith is mursal but accepted by Hanafis under conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۰۹) ومن لا ترجمه : (۸۰۶) [actually this is misaligned; correct reading from text: (۸۰۹) ومن لا جمعة عليه لو اداها جاز عن فرض الوقت] ترجمه : (۸۰۹) اور جن لوگوں پر جمعہ نہیں ہے اگر وہ جمعہ ادا کر لیں تو وقت کا فرض ، یعنی ظہر کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (۱) جمعہ اگر چہ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن ظہر اور جمعہ میں سے ایک ان پر واجب ہے۔ اس لئے اگر جمعہ پڑھ لیا تو ظہر کے بدلے میں ادا ہو جائے گا۔ (۲) یہ قول تابعی ان کی دلیل ہے . عن الحسن قال ان جمعن مع الامام اجزأهن من صلوة الامام. (مصنف ابن ابى هيبة ،۳۴۰ المرأة تشهد الجمعة اتجزيها صلوۃ الامام ، ص ۴۴۶، نمبر ۱۵۵۶ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب من جمعة عليه ان اداها جاز عن فرض الوقت - ص۷۴، نمبر ۵۲۱۹) (۳) روينا عن الحسن البصرى انه قال قد كن النساء يجمعن مع النبي ( سنن بیہقی ، باب من لا جمعہ علیہ اذ اشهد ها صلاها رکعتین ، ج ثالث ،ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۵۶۵۰) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عورت جمعہ پڑھے تو ظہر ادا ہو جائے گی، حالانکہ اس پر جمعہ نہیں ہے۔
(809) And those upon whom Jumu'ah is not obligatory, if they pray it, it suffices for the obligatory prayer of the time. Translation: (809) And those upon whom Jumu'ah is not obligatory, if they perform Jumu'ah, then the obligatory prayer of the time, i.e., Zuhr, will be fulfilled. Proof: (1) Even though Jumu'ah is not obligatory for them, but one of the two, Zuhr or Jumu'ah, is obligatory upon them. Therefore, if they pray Jumu'ah, it will be accepted in place of Zuhr. (2) This saying of the Tabi'i is their proof: From Hasan (al-Basri), he said: If they (women) gather with the imam, it suffices them from the prayer of the imam. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 340, al-Mar'ah tashhad al-jumu'ah atujziha salat al-imam, p. 446, no. 1556; Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, Bab man jumu'ah alayhi in adaha jaza an fard al-waqt, p. 74, no. 5219) (3) We have narrated from Hasan al-Basri that he said: Women used to gather for Jumu'ah with the Prophet. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man la jumu'ata alayhi idha shahidaha sallaha rak'atayn, vol. 3, p. 265, no. 5650) In this hadith it is that a woman prays Jumu'ah, then Zuhr will be fulfilled, even though Jumu'ah is not obligatory upon her.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage addresses those upon whom Jumu'ah is not originally obligatory, such as women, travellers, and the sick (according to Hanafi fiqh). The ruling is that if such a person chooses to pray Jumu'ah, it suffices them for the obligatory Zuhr prayer of that time. The reasoning (وجه) is that although Jumu'ah is not individually required of them, each Muslim must perform either Zuhr or Jumu'ah as the day's fard. By praying Jumu'ah, they fulfil that obligation. The proof includes a statement from Hasan al-Basri, a prominent Tabi'i, that women who prayed with the imam on Friday had that count as their obligation. Additionally, a hadith in Bayhaqi confirms that women used to pray Jumu'ah with the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) and it was valid. This principle is important: it shows the interchangeability of Zuhr and Jumu'ah for those not originally obligated, making Jumu'ah a valid substitute.

Key Terms
فرض الوقت (fard al-waqt): The obligatory prayer of the time, which is Zuhr on Friday for those not obligated to Jumu'ah.

D) Analogy with two rak'at

Key Takeaway
Jumu'ah, even for those not originally obligated, fulfills the Friday obligatory prayer and replaces Zuhr.

Ruling on Praying Zuhr Before Jumu'ah Without Excuse
Ruling on praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah for those without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without an excuse and identify the three proofs that support it.

Core Idea
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is makruh tahrimi, but the Zuhr prayer is valid.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a person obligated to attend Jumu'ah instead prays Zuhr before the Friday prayer. The primary text (matn) states 'haram', but the commentary from Al-Hidayah clarifies it is makruh (disliked). We will examine why it is disliked, the proofs behind this ruling, and the practical consequence that the Zuhr prayer still counts, though it should not have been done.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the initial ruling
The act is praying the Zuhr prayer before the Friday Jumu'ah prayer for a person who has no valid excuse (i.e., must attend Jumu'ah). The matn says it is 'haram' (forbidden).
The initial wording is strong, but later scholars softened it.
2
Note the relied-upon ruling from Hidayah
Imam al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah states it is 'makruh' (disliked), not haram. The preferred view is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The difference between haram and makruh tahrimi lies in the definitiveness of the proof.
3
Examine the three proofs cited
Three proofs are provided: (1) The hadith of Tariq ibn Shihab: 'Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation.' (2) The hadith of Abu al-Ja'd: 'Whoever neglects three Jumu'ahs carelessly, Allah seals his heart.' (3) The Quranic command 'fas'au ila dhikrillah' (hasten to the remembrance of Allah), which indicates obligation.
These proofs show the importance of Jumu'ah, but they are not definitive enough to make the act haram in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the practical consequence
Despite the dislike, the Zuhr prayer is valid because the original obligation for Friday is still Zuhr; Jumu'ah is a substitute. The person has fulfilled his obligation, albeit in a disliked manner.
If someone prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, he should not join Jumu'ah later, as it would create confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۱۰) ومن لا عذر له لو صلى الظهر قبلها حرم۔ ترجمه : (۸۱۰) جنکو عذر نہیں ہے اگر جمعہ سے پہلے ظہر پڑھ لی تو حرام ہے۔ تشریح : جسکو عذر نہیں ہے انکو جمعہ پڑھنا چاہئے لیکن جمعہ سے پہلے ظہر پڑھ لیا تو مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اصل سے احتراز کیا۔ ھدایہ میں مکر وہ لکھا ہے۔ وجه (۱) مکروہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبي الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة للملوك والمرأة ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جمعہ ہر مسلمان پر بشرط مذکورہ واجب ہے۔ اس لئے بغیر عذر کے ظہر کی نماز امام کی نماز سے پہلے پڑھی تو مکروہ ہے (۲) دوسری حدیث ہے عن ابي الجعد الضمرى وكانت له صحبة ان رسول الله الله قال من ترك ثلاث جمع تهاونا بها طبع الله على قلبه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب التهديد فی ترک الجمعۃ ص ۱۵۸ نمبر ۱۰۵۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی تین جمعہ بغیر عذر کے چھوڑ دے تو اللہ اس کے دل پر مہر لگا دیتے ہیں۔ اس لئے بغیر عذر کے ظہر کی نماز امام سے پہلے پڑھ لی تو مکروہ ہے (۳) فاسعوا الى ذكر الله میں فاسعوا امر وجوب کے لئے ہے۔ اور انہوں نے بغیر عذر کے امر کو چھوڑا اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ چونکہ اصل میں ظہر ہی ہے اس لئے ظہر کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔
(810) And he who has no excuse, if he prays Zuhr before it (Jumu'ah), it is forbidden (haram). Translation: (810) Those who have no excuse, if they pray Zuhr before Jumu'ah, then it is forbidden. Explanation: One who has no excuse should pray Jumu'ah. But if he prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, it is disliked (makruh). Because he avoided the original (Jumu'ah). In Hidayah, it is written as makruh. Proof: (1) The reason for it being makruh is this hadith: From Tariq ibn Shihab from the Prophet (peace be upon him): Jumu'ah is a right obligatory upon every Muslim in congregation. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Jumu'ah lil-muluk wal-mar'ah, p. 120, no. 1067) From this hadith it is known that Jumu'ah is obligatory upon every Muslim with the mentioned condition. Therefore, without excuse, praying Zuhr before the imam's prayer is makruh. (2) Another hadith: From Abu al-Ja'd al-Damari, who was a Companion, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Whoever neglects three Jumu'ahs carelessly, Allah will seal his heart. (Abu Dawud, Bab al-tahdid fi tark al-jumu'ah, p. 158, no. 1052) This hadith also shows that if someone neglects three Jumu'ahs without excuse, Allah seals his heart. Hence, without excuse, praying Zuhr before the imam is makruh. (3) In the verse 'فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله' (Hasten to the remembrance of Allah), the word 'fas'au' is a command for obligation. And they, without excuse, have left the command, so it is makruh. However, since the original obligation is Zuhr, the Zuhr prayer is still fulfilled.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This lesson deals with the ruling for a person who is obligated to pray Jumu'ah (i.e., free, male, resident, etc.) but chooses to pray Zuhr before the Friday prayer. The initial matn uses the word 'حرم' (forbidden), but the commentary clarifies that according to the Hidayah, it is makruh (disliked) rather than haram. The reason is that Jumu'ah is a right upon every Muslim, and neglecting it without excuse is condemned. The hadith of Tariq ibn Shihab states Jumu'ah is 'حق واجب' (a necessary right), implying it is wajib. Another hadith threatens sealing the heart for missing three Jumu'ahs. The Quranic command 'فاسعوا' (hasten) is understood as a command of obligation. However, despite the dislike, the Zuhr prayer is still valid because the original obligation for the day is Zuhr, and Jumu'ah is a substitute. So the person must still perform the Zuhr he prayed; if he later joins Jumu'ah, it would be problematic. The commentary notes that the Hidayah says 'مکروہ' (makruh), so the correct term is makruh tanzih or tahrimi? The text does not specify, but given the strength of the proofs, it could be makruh tahrimi. However, the presence of the word 'حرم' in the matn might be a typo or stronger expression. The overall position is that it is severely disliked and should be avoided.

Key Terms
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): An action that is prohibitively disliked, close to haram, but without a definitive proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what is the relied-upon ruling for praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without an excuse?
A) Haram
B) Makruh
C) Mubah
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Praying Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is makruh tahrimi, yet the prayer is valid because Jumu'ah is a substitute for the original Zuhr.

Proceeding to Jumu'ah After Zuhr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidity of Zuhr by proceeding to Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the invalidity of Zuhr when one proceeds to Jumu'ah after praying Zuhr, and apply Imam Abu Hanifa's principle to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Participating in the beginning of an act equals participating in the whole act — the key principle driving this dispute.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens to a person who prays Zuhr on Friday and then immediately sets out to catch Jumu'ah, but the imam is already deep into the prayer? The central question is whether the mere act of walking to the mosque invalidates the already-offered Zuhr. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, differ sharply. Understanding their disagreement illuminates the school's methodology of deriving rulings from general principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the disputed ruling
The scenario: a person prays Zuhr, then proceeds (sa'y) to Jumu'ah while the imam is already praying. The dispute: does the Zuhr become invalid if the person does not catch the Jumu'ah?
Note the timing: after Zuhr, during the imam's prayer.
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position and his principle
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the Zuhr becomes invalid immediately upon proceeding, even if one misses Jumu'ah. His principle: participation in the beginning of an act is like participation in the entire act. Walking to Jumu'ah is a distinctive part of Jumu'ah, so it is akin to having joined the prayer.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on a general principle.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their reasoning
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only actual joining (catching a rak'ah) invalidates Zuhr; mere proceeding does not. They require actual participation in the prayer itself.
Their view is more literal and pragmatic.
4
Analyze the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the person proceeds but misses Jumu'ah: Abu Hanifa requires redoing Zuhr; the Sahibayn say Zuhr remains valid. If he catches Jumu'ah, both agree Zuhr is invalid.
The consequence only differs when Jumu'ah is missed.
5
Evaluate the authority and practical application
The text does not give explicit tarjih, but later Hanafi practice often prefers the Sahibayn's position for practicality. The mufta bihi in many fatwa collections follows the Sahibayn.
Always check the relied-upon view in your context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۱۱) فان سعى اليها والامام فيها بطل ظهره وان لم يدركها۔ ترجمه : (۸۱۱) پس اگر جمعہ کی طرف سعی کی اور امام جمعہ میں ہے تو اس کا ظہر باطل ہو جائے گا، اگر چہ جمعہ نہ پائے۔ تشریح : ظہر پڑھنے کے بعد جمعہ کی طرف سعی کی ، اور امام جمعہ کی نماز میں تھے تو چاہے ظہر نہ پایا ہوتب بھی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزد یک ظہر باطل ہو جائے گا، اب اگر جمعہ مل گیا تب تو وہ ادا ہو گیا، اور جمعہ نہ ملا تو ظہر دوبارہ پڑھے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جمعہ مل گیا تب تو ظہر باطل ہوگا، اور جمعہ نہ ملا تو صرف اس کی طرف سعی کرنے سے ظہر باطل نہیں ہو گا۔ وجه : (۱) امام ابوحنیفہ کا اصول یہ ہے کہ ابتداء شی ء میں شریک ہونا گویا کہ اصل شی ء میں شریک ہونا ہے۔اسی اصول پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنا [ چلنا ] جمعہ کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے اور اس نے گھر سے چل کر سعی کی تو گویا کہ جمعہ کا ابتدائی حصہ پالیا تو گویا کہ جمعہ میں شریک ہو گیا اور ابھی اوپر گزرا کہ جمعہ میں شریک ہو جائے تو ظہر باطل ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنے سے ظہر باطل ہو جائے گا۔
(811) So if he proceeds to it (Jumu'ah) while the imam is in it, his Zuhr becomes invalid even if he does not catch it. Translation: (811) So if he makes effort to go to Jumu'ah and the imam is in (the prayer of) Jumu'ah, then his Zuhr becomes invalid, even if he does not catch the Jumu'ah. Explanation: After praying Zuhr, he proceeded to Jumu'ah, and the imam was in the Jumu'ah prayer; then even if he did not catch the (rak'ah of) Jumu'ah, according to Imam Abu Hanifa, his Zuhr becomes invalid. Now, if he catches Jumu'ah, then it is fulfilled; if he does not catch Jumu'ah, then he must repeat Zuhr. And the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: If he catches Jumu'ah, then his Zuhr becomes invalid; but if he does not catch Jumu'ah, then merely proceeding towards it does not invalidate his Zuhr. Proof: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa's principle is that participating in the beginning of something is like participating in the thing itself. This issue is based on that principle. He says that proceeding towards Jumu'ah (walking) is among the special features of Jumu'ah, and when he walked from home and proceeded, it is as if he obtained the initial part of Jumu'ah, so he has become a participant in Jumu'ah. And it has passed earlier that if one participates in Jumu'ah, his Zuhr becomes invalid. Therefore, by merely proceeding towards Jumu'ah, his Zuhr becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding a person who prays Zuhr (on Friday) and then, after praying, proceeds to the mosque while the imam is already leading the Jumu'ah prayer. The question is: does the act of proceeding (سعى) invalidate the previously prayed Zuhr? Imam Abu Hanifa rules that the Zuhr becomes invalid even if the person does not actually catch the Jumu'ah prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the Zuhr only becomes invalid if the person actually catches the Jumu'ah prayer (i.e., joins the congregation), but mere walking towards it does not invalidate. The reasoning (وجه) given for Imam Abu Hanifa's position is his well-known principle: participating in the beginning of an act is equivalent to participating in the entire act. Since proceeding (walking) to Jumu'ah is part of its rituals, starting the journey is like starting the prayer itself. Therefore, by starting to go, the person has effectively entered into Jumu'ah, and since attending Jumu'ah invalidates a previously prayed Zuhr (as established in earlier rulings), his Zuhr is invalidated. If he then catches the Jumu'ah, it suffices; if he misses it, he must redo Zuhr. The practical consequence is significant: for Abu Hanifa, once one sets out for Jumu'ah after praying Zuhr, the Zuhr is no longer valid; for the Sahibayn, only actual joining invalidates. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) typically follows the Sahibayn in the Hanafi school, but the text does not explicitly state tarjih here.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): Here it means proceeding or making an effort to go to Jumu'ah, including walking.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two disciples: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the primary students of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a person prays Zuhr on Friday and then starts walking to the mosque while the imam is in Jumu'ah prayer, but misses the Jumu'ah, what is the status of his Zuhr?
A) It remains valid
B) It becomes invalid and must be repeated
C) It becomes a nafl prayer
D) It is valid but Makruh

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa's principle that participating in the beginning of an act is like participating in the whole act leads to the invalidity of Zuhr upon proceeding to Jumu'ah, while the Sahibayn require actual joining.

Performing Zuhr Before Jumu'ah Without Excuse
Ruling on the prohibition of Zuhr before Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse, explain the evidence, and distinguish between makruh tahrimi and haram.

Core Idea
Performing Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is valid but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a common Friday scenario: a person without a valid excuse prays Zuhr before the Jumu'ah prayer begins. The text presents the ruling, clarifies that it is not haram but makruh tahrimi, and provides three proofs to support this position. By understanding the reasoning, you will grasp how the Hanafi school balances obligations and exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (Zuhr before Jumu'ah) and the initial hukm term used ('haram'). Then note the commentator's clarification that the actual ruling is makruh tahrimi.
The matn uses 'haram' but al-Hidayah clarifies it is makruh tahrimi due to the evidence being zanni.
2
Locate the dalil
Three proofs are cited: (1) Hadith of Tariq ibn Shihab stating Jumu'ah is 'haqqun wajib', (2) Hadith of Abu al-Ja'd threatening those who abandon three Jumu'ahs, (3) Quranic command 'fasa'u' from Surah al-Jumu'ah. Identify each as a dalil for the obligation of Jumu'ah.
All are ahad and zanni al-thubut, which influences the hukm level.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'haqqun wajib' indicates obligation. Hanafi usul treats such command as indicating wujub (obligation) but not fard because the hadith is ahad. The two other proofs reinforce the seriousness of missing Jumu'ah.
Wujub is a level below fard; violation leads to sin but not to the same degree as fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that the Shafi'i school considers missing Jumu'ah without excuse as haram (forbidden). This difference stems from their classification of the evidence as qat'i or zanni.
Hanafis consider the evidence zanni, hence makruh tahrimi; Shafi'is consider it qat'i, hence haram.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is makruh tahrimi, as recorded in al-Hidayah and confirmed by the commentator. The Zuhr prayer remains valid because Jumu'ah is a substitute (badal) for Zuhr.
Tarjih authority: al-Hidayah (zahir al-riwayah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن لا عذر له لو صلى الظهر قبلها حرم
ترجمه : (۸۱۰) جنکو عذر نہیں ہے اگر جمعہ سے پہلے ظہر پڑھ لی تو حرام ہے۔
تشریح : جسکو عذر نہیں ہے انکو جمعہ پڑھنا چاہئے لیکن جمعہ سے پہلے ظہر پڑھ لیا تو مکروہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے اصل سے احتراز کیا۔ ھدایہ میں مکر وہ لکھا ہے۔
وجه (۱) مکروہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن طارق بن شهاب عن النبي الله قال الجمعة حق واجب على كل مسلم في جماعة (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الجمعة للملوك والمرأة ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۱۰۶۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جمعہ ہر مسلمان پر بشرط مذکورہ واجب ہے۔ اس لئے بغیر عذر کے ظہر کی نماز امام کی نماز سے پہلے پڑھی تو مکروہ ہے (۲) دوسری حدیث ہے عن ابي الجعد الضمرى وكانت له صحبة ان رسول الله الله قال من ترك ثلاث جمع تهاونا بها طبع الله على قلبه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب التهديد فی ترک الجمعۃ ص ۱۵۸ نمبر ۱۰۵۲) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی تین جمعہ بغیر عذر کے چھوڑ دے تو اللہ اس کے دل پر مہر لگا دیتے ہیں۔ اس لئے بغیر عذر کے ظہر کی نماز امام سے پہلے پڑھ لی تو مکروہ ہے (۳) فاسعوا الى ذكر الله میں فاسعوا امر وجوب کے لئے ہے۔ اور انہوں نے بغیر عذر کے امر کو چھوڑا اس لئے مکروہ ہے۔ البتہ چونکہ اصل میں ظہر ہی ہے اس لئے ظہر کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔
And whoever has no excuse, if he prays Zuhr before it (Jumu'ah), it is forbidden. Translation: (810) For those who have no excuse, if they perform Zuhr before Jumu'ah, it is forbidden. Explanation: Those who have no excuse should pray Jumu'ah, but if they perform Zuhr before Jumu'ah, it is disliked (makruh). Because they avoided the original. In Hidayah, it is written as makruh. Reason (1) The reason for being disliked is this hadith: From Tariq ibn Shihab from the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Jumu'ah is a right and an obligation upon every Muslim in congregation.' (Abu Dawud) From this hadith it is understood that Jumu'ah is obligatory upon every Muslim with the mentioned condition. Therefore, without excuse, performing Zuhr prayer before the Imam's prayer is disliked. (2) Second hadith: From Abu al-Ja'd al-Damari, who was a Companion, that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever abandons three Jumu'ahs out of negligence, Allah will seal his heart.' (Abu Dawud) From this hadith also it is understood that if someone leaves three Jumu'ahs without excuse, Allah seals his heart. Therefore, without excuse, performing Zuhr before the Imam is disliked. (3) In 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah' (Surah al-Jumu'ah), the word 'fasa'u' is a command for obligation. And they left the command without excuse, so it is disliked. However, since the original is Zuhr, the Zuhr prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The matn states a general prohibition: 'Whoever has no excuse, if he prays Zuhr before Jumu'ah, it is forbidden.' The commentator explains that this refers to makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) according to the Hanafi school, as clarified in al-Hidayah. The ruling is supported by three proofs: (1) The hadith of Tariq ibn Shihab establishing Jumu'ah as wajib; (2) The hadith threatening those who abandon three Jumu'ahs; (3) The Quranic command 'fasa'u' implying obligation. Despite the prohibition, the Zuhr prayer is valid because Jumu'ah is an alternative (badal) to Zuhr, and the original obligation is still fulfilled. The key point is that one should not deliberately avoid Jumu'ah without a valid excuse.

Key Terms
عذر ('udhr): A valid excuse that exempts one from Jumu'ah, such as illness, fear, or rain.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): Something prohibitively disliked; sinful but not as severe as haram, based on zanni evidence.
حق واجب (haqqun wajib): A right and an obligation; indicates a binding duty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The Zuhr prayer is valid but prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
C) The Zuhr prayer is invalid and the person must perform Jumu'ah instead.

Key Takeaway
Performing Zuhr before Jumu'ah without excuse is valid but prohibitively disliked because Jumu'ah is wajib and one should not neglect it.

Going to Jumu'ah After Having Prayed Zuhr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidation of Zuhr by proceeding to Jumu'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the invalidation of Zuhr when one proceeds to Jumu'ah, and apply the principles underlying their disagreement.

Core Idea
Proceeding to Jumu'ah after Zuhr: for Abu Hanifa, the beginning is like the whole; for Sahibayn, only actual joining invalidates.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. If a person prays Zuhr on Friday and then walks to the mosque for Jumu'ah, does that Zuhr become invalid even if they do not catch the Jumu'ah? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, because proceeding is like joining the beginning. The Sahibayn disagree, holding that only actual participation in Jumu'ah can invalidate the substitute. Understanding this disagreement helps illuminate deeper usul principles about how the Hanafi school weighs obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the dispute
Identify the act: a person prays Zuhr on Friday, then proceeds (sa'y) to Jumu'ah while the Imam is already in prayer. The dispute is whether the Zuhr becomes invalid if the person does not actually catch the Jumu'ah.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's principle
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that participating in the beginning of a thing is like participating in the thing itself (بداءة الشيء كالاشتراك فيه). Proceeding is a characteristic of Jumu'ah, so it is like joining.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's opposing principle
The Sahibayn hold that the substitute (Zuhr) is only invalidated when one fully attains the original (Jumu'ah). Mere proceeding is not attainment.
4
Trace the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If one proceeds but does not catch Jumu'ah, Abu Hanifa says Zuhr is invalid and must be repeated; Sahibayn say Zuhr remains valid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the Hanafi school is Imam Abu Hanifa's, as it is more cautious in preserving the sanctity of Jumu'ah.

Source Text

فان سعى اليها والامام فيها بطل ظهره وان لم يدركها
ترجمه : (۸۱۱) پس اگر جمعہ کی طرف سعی کی اور امام جمعہ میں ہے تو اس کا ظہر باطل ہو جائے گا، اگر چہ جمعہ نہ پائے۔
تشریح : ظہر پڑھنے کے بعد جمعہ کی طرف سعی کی ، اور امام جمعہ کی نماز میں تھے تو چاہے ظہر نہ پایا ہوتب بھی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزد یک ظہر باطل ہو جائے گا، اب اگر جمعہ مل گیا تب تو وہ ادا ہو گیا، اور جمعہ نہ ملا تو ظہر دوبارہ پڑھے۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جمعہ مل گیا تب تو ظہر باطل ہوگا، اور جمعہ نہ ملا تو صرف اس کی طرف سعی کرنے سے ظہر باطل نہیں ہو گا۔
وجه : (۱) امام ابوحنیفہ کا اصول یہ ہے کہ ابتداء شی ء میں شریک ہونا گویا کہ اصل شی ء میں شریک ہونا ہے۔اسی اصول پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنا [ چلنا ] جمعہ کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے اور اس نے گھر سے چل کر سعی کی تو گویا کہ جمعہ کا ابتدائی حصہ پالیا تو گویا کہ جمعہ میں شریک ہو گیا اور ابھی اوپر گزرا کہ جمعہ میں شریک ہو جائے تو ظہر باطل ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنے سے ظہر باطل ہو جائے گا۔
صاحبین کا اصول یہ ہے کہ اصل پر پورے طور پر قادر ہو گا تب ہی فرع باطل ہو گا۔ اب جمعہ کی طرف سعی اصل نہیں ہے یہ تو اصل سے بہت پہلے کی چیز ہے جمعہ اس کے کافی دیر بعد ہے اسلئے جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنے سے ظہر باطل نہیں ہوگا ، ہاں اصل جمعہ میں شریک ہو جائے تب ظہر باطل ہوگا، کیونکہ اصل پر قدرت سے بدل باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔۔ اور ظہر کے باطل ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر چھوڑ کر جمعہ پڑھنے کے لئے کہا تو جمعہ اعلی ہوا ، اسلئے اعلی پر قدرت کی وجہ سے ادنی باطل ہو جائے گا
اصول : امام ابو حنیفہ کے یہاں ابتداء شی کو بعض مرتبہ اصل کا درجہ دیا جاتا ہے۔
اصول : صاحبین کے یہاں بالکل اصل پر جب تک قدرت نہ ہو بدل باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
Then if he goes towards it (Jumu'ah) and the Imam is in it, his Zuhr becomes invalid even if he does not catch it. Translation: (811) So if he proceeded to Jumu'ah and the Imam is in the prayer, his Zuhr becomes invalid, even if he does not catch the Jumu'ah. Explanation: After praying Zuhr, he proceeded to Jumu'ah. If the Imam was in the prayer, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa, his Zuhr becomes invalid even if he did not catch the Jumu'ah. If he catches Jumu'ah, then it is performed; if not, he must repeat Zuhr. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say: If he catches Jumu'ah, then Zuhr becomes invalid; but if he does not catch it, merely proceeding to Jumu'ah does not invalidate Zuhr. Reason: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa's principle is that participating in the beginning of a thing is like participating in the thing itself. Proceeding to Jumu'ah is one of its characteristics; by walking from home, he has caught the initial part, so he is considered to have joined Jumu'ah. And it passed earlier that if one joins Jumu'ah, his Zuhr becomes invalid. Therefore, proceeding to Jumu'ah invalidates Zuhr. The Sahibayn's principle is that only when one fully attains the original does the substitute become invalid. Proceeding to Jumu'ah is not the original; it is something before the original. Jumu'ah comes much later. So merely proceeding does not invalidate Zuhr. Yes, if he catches the actual Jumu'ah, then Zuhr becomes invalid because having power over the original invalidates the substitute. The reason for invalidation is that on Friday, one is commanded to leave Zuhr and pray Jumu'ah, so Jumu'ah is superior; having power over the superior invalidates the inferior. Principle: For Imam Abu Hanifa, initiating a thing is sometimes given the status of the original. Principle: For the Sahibayn, until one has full power over the original, the substitute is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The issue: If a person prays Zuhr on Friday and then proceeds to the Jumu'ah prayer, does the Zuhr become invalid if he does not actually catch the Jumu'ah? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, because proceeding to Jumu'ah is like participating in the beginning of it, which is treated as joining the prayer. The Sahibayn say no; only actual catching of Jumu'ah invalidates Zuhr. The reliance (mufta bihi) is typically on Abu Hanifa's view in the Hanafi school, as it is more precautionary. The passage also points out that if one catches Jumu'ah, all agree that Zuhr is invalidated.

Key Terms
سعی (sa'y): Proceeding or going towards the Jumu'ah prayer; the act of walking to the mosque.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, major disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Catching Jumu'ah in Tashahhud or Sajda Sahw
Ruling on catching Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajda sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajda sahw and explain the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Catching Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajda sahw suffices for validity in the Hanafi school.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: arriving late for Jumu'ah and joining when the Imam is in tashahhud or performing sajda sahw. Is your prayer valid? The Hanafi school gives a clear ruling based on the principle that catching any part of the prayer counts as catching the congregation. We will explore this ruling, its basis, and how it contrasts with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the matn: it says whoever catches Jumu'ah in tashahhud or sajda sahw should complete his Jumu'ah. The ruling is that his prayer is valid and he must finish the remaining rak'ahs after the imam gives salam.
This is a clear statement of the Hanafi position.
2
Understand the underlying principle
The Hanafi school holds that catching any part of the prayer—even the final tashahhud or sajda sahw—counts as catching the prayer itself. This is based on the idea that the prayer is a single continuous act, so joining at any point makes one a participant.
This contrasts with schools that require catching a full rak'ah.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i requires catching at least one rak'ah (the bowing and prostration) for the prayer to count. Catching only tashahhud would not be sufficient in his school; the latecomer would instead pray Zuhr.
The practical consequence: a Hanafi latecomer can pray Jumu'ah, while a Shafi'i would miss Jumu'ah.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider: A person arrives at the mosque and finds the imam in the final tashahhud. According to the Hanafi school, he should say takbir, sit down, and after the imam's salam, stand up and complete the remaining two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah.
If he arrived during sajda sahw, the same rule applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من ادركها في التشهد او في سجود السهو فليتم جمعته
ترجمه : (۸۱۳) جس نے جمعہ کو تشہد میں پایا ، یا سجدہ سہو میں پایا تو وہ جمعہ پورا کرے۔ واللہ اعلم۔
And whoever catches it (Jumu'ah) in tashahhud or in sajda sahw, he should complete his Jumu'ah. Translation: (813) Whoever catches Jumu'ah during tashahhud or sajda sahw should complete his Jumu'ah. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the matn. It states that a person who joins the Jumu'ah prayer while the Imam is in the final tashahhud or while performing sajda sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is considered to have caught the prayer. Therefore, he should complete the remaining rak'ahs of Jumu'ah (i.e., pray the missed part after the Imam ends) and his Jumu'ah is valid. This is based on the principle that catching any part of the prayer, including the tashahhud, is sufficient to count as having caught the congregation.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The sitting in prayer for recitation of the testimony of faith; the final tashahhud of the prayer.
سجود السهو (sajda sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) He must make sajda sahw to complete his Jumu'ah.
D) Jumu'ah is not valid for him; he must pray four rak'ahs of Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, catching any part of Jumu'ah, even tashahhud or sajda sahw, counts as catching the prayer and obligates completing the rak'ahs.

Ruling on Zuhr in Congregation for the Excused and Prisoners on Friday
Ruling with proofs and intra-Hanafi usul discussion on substitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday for those excused from Jumu'ah, identify the evidence from the athar, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on when the substitute becomes invalid due to intention.

Core Idea
Performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday is disliked but valid; the substitute's invalidity depends on actual participation, not mere intention, according to the Sahibayn.

This lesson examines the ruling (hukm) for those who are excused from attending Jumu'ah or are imprisoned: may they pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday? The text declares it makruh (disliked) but valid, and then explores a key usul principle: when does the substitute prayer (Zuhr) become invalid if one intends to attend Jumu'ah? This intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, deepens our understanding of legal substitution (badal) and the weight of intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and the hukm level: performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday for the excused or imprisoned. The text says it is 'makruh' (disliked) but valid if done.
Dislikedness is makruh tanzihi, not haram.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
Find the athar cited in the text: from al-Hasan, 'Ali, Ibrahim, and Ibn Sirin. Note the type (mursal) and its content that supports the dislike.
The athar from al-Hasan explicitly uses the word 'karaha'.
3
Extract the reasoning from the commentary
Understand the commentator's explanation: Jumu'ah is superior and takes precedence; therefore, even those not obliged should not form congregations for Zuhr as it undermines Jumu'ah's importance.
The counter-evidence from Ibn Sirin shows permissibility for prisoners, but the Hanafi position prefers not doing so.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on substitution
Identify the point of ikhtilaf: When does the substitute (Zuhr) become invalid due to ability for the original (Jumu'ah)? Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the beginning of the act (intention/setting out) can have the status of the original; the Sahibayn require actual participation.
This is a pure usul disagreement; both views are presented without a final tarjih.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If a ma'dhur intends to go for Jumu'ah but then prays Zuhr, according to Abu Hanifa the Zuhr might be invalid, while according to the Sahibayn it remains valid until he actually joins Jumu'ah.
The ruling on dislike is agreed upon; the dispute affects only the validity of the prayer under specific conditions.

(۸۱۲) وكره للمعذور والمسجون اداء الظهر بجماعة في المصر يومها
صاحبين کا اصول یہ ہے کہ اصل پر پورے طور پر قادر ہو گا تب ہی فرع باطل ہو گا۔ اب جمعہ کی طرف سعی اصل نہیں ہے یہ تو اصل سے بہت پہلے کی چیز ہے جمعہ اس کے کافی دیر بعد ہے اسلئے جمعہ کی طرف سعی کرنے سے ظہر باطل نہیں ہوگا ، ہاں اصل جمعہ میں شریک ہو جائے تب ظہر باطل ہوگا، کیونکہ اصل پر قدرت سے بدل باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔۔ اور ظہر کے باطل ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے دن ظہر چھوڑ کر جمعہ پڑھنے کے لئے کہا تو جمعہ اعلی ہوا ، اسلئے اعلی پر قدرت کی وجہ سے ادنی باطل ہو جائے گا
اصول : امام ابو حنیفہ کے یہاں ابتداء شی کو بعض مرتبہ اصل کا درجہ دے دیا جاتا ہے۔ اصول : صاحبین کے یہاں بالکل اصل پر جب تک قدرت نہ ہو بدل باطل نہیں ہوگا۔
ترجمه : (۸۱۲) معذور اور قیدیوں کے لئے جمعہ کے دن شہر میں جماعت کے ساتھ ظہر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح : جمعہ کے دن جمعہ کی نماز پڑھنی چاہیئے اس لئے اس کی اہمیت کے لئے معذور اور قیدیوں کے لئے بھی جماعت کے ساتھ ظہر پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ تا ہم پڑھ لی تو جائز ہے۔
وجه : (۱) عن الحسن انه كان يكره اذا لم يدرك قوم الجمعة ان يصلوا الجماعة . (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القوم يا تون المسجد يوم الجمعة بعد انصراف الناس، ج ثالث ص ۱۲۰ نمبر ۵۴۷۳) (۲) اور مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ میں ہے قال على لا جماعة يوم الجمعة الا مع الامام - (مصنف ابن ابی هیپه [؟] ۳۷۴ فی القوم تجمعون يوم الجمعة اذالم يشهد وها، ج اول، ص ۴۶۶، نمبر ۵۳۹۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جمعہ کے دن معذورین کو جماعت کے ساتھ ظہر نہیں پڑھنا چاہئے ۔ (۳) اور قیدی لوگ جیل خانے میں جمعہ نہ پڑھے اسکے لئے یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال : ليس على أهل السجون جمعة - (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب فی اهل السجون ، ج اول ص ۴۸۴، نمبر ۵۵۷۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قیدیوں پر جمعہ نہیں ہے (۴) دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ قید میں اذن عام نہیں ہوتی اسلئے بھی وہاں جمعہ نہیں ہے۔۔ (۵) لیکن دوسرے حضرات جیل میں جمعہ کے قائل ہیں، انکی دلیل یراثر ہے. عن ابن سيرين في اهل السجون قال : يجمعوا الصلوة يوم الجمعة ۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ، باب فی احل السجون، ج اول ، ص ۱۴۸۴، نمبر۷ ۵۵۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قید خانے میں جمعہ قائم کر سکتا ہے۔ سجن : قیدی۔ (۶) معذور جماعت نماز پڑھ لے تو نماز ہو جائے گی اس کے لئے یہ دلیل ہے۔ فـذکر زرو التیمـي [؟] فـي يوم جمعة ثم صلوا الجمعة اربعا فى مكانهم وكانوا خائفين (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۳۷۴ فی القوم مجمعون يوم الجمعۃ اذالم يشهد وھاج اول، ص ۴۶۶، نمبر ۵۳۹۵/مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب القوم یا تون المسجد يوم الجمعة بعد انصراف الناس، ج ثالث ص ۱۲۰، نمبر ۵۴۷۲ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ معذورین جماعت کے ساتھ ظہر پڑھے تو اتنی کراہیت نہیں ہے۔
(812) It is disliked for the excused and the imprisoned to perform Zuhr with congregation in the city on [Friday] its day. The principle of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that when one becomes fully capable of the original, then the substitute becomes invalid. Now, proceeding towards Jumu'ah is not the original; it is from much before the original; Jumu'ah is well after it. Therefore, proceeding towards Jumu'ah does not invalidate Zuhr. However, if he joins the actual Jumu'ah, then Zuhr becomes invalid, because with ability for the original, the substitute becomes invalid. And the reason for Zuhr's invalidity is that on Friday, Zuhr is left and Jumu'ah is commanded; thus Jumu'ah is superior; so due to ability for the superior, the inferior becomes invalid. Principle: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the beginning of a thing is sometimes given the status of the original. Principle: According to the two companions, as long as there is no ability for the actual original, the substitute will not become invalid. Translation: (812) It is disliked for the excused and the prisoners to perform Zuhr with congregation in the city on Friday. Explanation: On Friday, one should pray Jumu'ah; therefore, due to its importance, it is disliked for the excused and prisoners to pray Zuhr with congregation. However, if they do, it is permissible. Evidences: (1) From al-Hasan that he disliked when a group did not catch Jumu'ah that they pray in congregation. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...). (2) And in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: 'Ali said: There is no congregation on Friday except with the imam. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...). From this effect it is known that the excused should not pray Zuhr in congregation on Friday. (3) And for prisoners who do not pray Jumu'ah in jail, there is this effect: From Ibrahim: Jumu'ah is not obligatory on prison inmates. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...). (4) Another reason is that in prison there is no general permission, so Jumu'ah is not [obligatory]. (5) But others hold that Jumu'ah can be held in jail; their evidence is the effect: From Ibn Sirin regarding prison inmates: They may gather for prayer on Friday. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba...). (6) For the excused, if they pray congregation, the prayer is valid; the evidence is: Mentioned by Zurāra al-Tamīmī: On a Friday, they prayed Zuhr as four in their place while they were fearful. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq...). From this effect, it is known that if the excused pray Zuhr in congregation, such dislike is less.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with evidence and an intra-Hanafi principle discussion. The primary ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) for a person who is excused from Jumu'ah (e.g., due to travel, illness) and for a prisoner to perform Zuhr prayer in congregation in a city on Friday. However, if they do so, the prayer is valid (jā'iz). The commentator explains the basis: Jumu'ah takes precedence on Friday, so even those not obliged to attend should not form congregations for Zuhr, as this undermines the importance of Jumu'ah. The text then delves into an usul (legal principle) dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The context is the substitution of Zuhr with Jumu'ah: if one intends to go for Jumu'ah, does that intention render a Zuhr prayer already begun invalid? The Sahibayn hold that only actual participation in Jumu'ah invalidates the Zuhr, not mere intention or proceeding. Imam Abu Hanifa sometimes gives the beginning of an action (like setting out) the status of the original, so even intending may invalidate the substitute. The commentary then provides several athar (narrations from Companions/Tabi'in) as evidence for the dislike. Notably, a narration from Hasan al-Basri dislikes congregation for those who missed Jumu'ah, and from 'Ali that there is no congregation on Friday except with the imam. For prisoners, an athar from Ibrahim says Jumu'ah is not on them, but another from Ibn Sirin permits them to gather. The overall point: the dislikedness is not severe; it is makruh tanzihi (not approaching haram).

Key Terms
معذور (ma'dhur): A person who has a valid excuse (e.g., travel, illness) that exempts them from Jumu'ah attendance.
مسجون (masjun): A prisoner; one who is incarcerated and cannot attend Jumu'ah due to confinement.
بدل (badal): Substitute; here Zuhr prayer on Friday serves as a substitute for Jumu'ah when Jumu'ah is not attended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a prisoner performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday according to this passage?
A) It is haram and invalid
B) It is makruh (disliked) but valid
C) It is wajib for him to pray Zuhr
D) It is sunnah mu'akkadah

Key Takeaway
Performing Zuhr in congregation on Friday is makruh tanzih for those excused from Jumu'ah, and the dispute over when the substitute becomes invalid does not affect the basic validity of the prayer.

Catching Jumu'ah Before Salam: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with hadith proofs on joining Jumu'ah late

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on catching Jumu'ah before salam and apply the hadith proof to determine the latecomer's prayer.

Core Idea
Catching Jumu'ah before salam means you pray Jumu'ah, not Zuhr.

This passage addresses a critical question: at what point does a latecomer count as having caught the Jumu'ah prayer? The Hanafi school holds that even joining the imam in the final sitting (tashahhud) or during the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) is sufficient to complete the prayer as Jumu'ah. This ruling is supported by two key hadith proofs, which we will examine to understand the evidence behind the position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Clearly state what act is being ruled upon (catching Jumu'ah before salam) and the ruling (complete it as Jumu'ah, not Zuhr).
The act is joining the imam in tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw.
2
Locate the Dalil
Identify the two hadith cited: the general command from Abu Hurairah (Bukhari, Muslim) and the specific hadith from Darqutni.
The general hadith says 'pray what you catch, complete what you miss.'
3
Examine the Wajh al-Dalalah
Analyze how the hadiths prove the ruling. The general hadith indicates that catching any part of the prayer counts; the specific hadith confirms that sitting with the imam before salam is sufficient.
The Hanafi interpretation emphasizes the literal command.
4
Note Cross-Madhhab Difference
Recognize that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require catching at least one rak'ah for Jumu'ah to be valid.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is when a latecomer arrives in the final sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۱۳) ومن ادركها في التشهد او سجود السهو اتم جمعة . والله اعلم
ترجمه : (۸۱۳) جس نے جمعہ کو تشہد میں پایا ، یا سجدہ سہو میں پایا تو وہ جمعہ پورا کرے۔ واللہ اعلم۔
تشریح : جمعہ کو تشہد میں یا سجدہ سہو میں پایا، حاصل یہ کہ سلام سے پہلے امام کے ساتھ مل گیا تو اب اس پر بنا کر کے جمعہ پڑھے گا ظہر نہیں پڑھے گا۔
وجه (۱) دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابى هريرة عن النبي الله قال اذا سمعتم الاقامة فامشوا الى الصلوة وعليكم السكينة والوقار ولا تسرعوا فما ادركتم فصلوا وما فاتكم فاتموا . (بخاری شریف، باب لا یسعی الی الصلوۃ ولیا تھا بالسکینۃ والوقار ص ۸۸ نمبر ۶۳۶ ر مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب اتيان الصلوة بوقار وسكينة ، والنھی عن استيا نها سعيا ،ص ۲۴۳، نمبر ۱۳۵۹/۶۰۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جتنا ملا وہ امام کے ساتھ پڑھو اور جتنا فوت ہو گیا اس کو اسی پر بنا کر لو، تو امام کے ساتھ سلام سے پہلے ملاتو انتا امام کے ساتھ پڑھے گا اور باقی کا اسی پر بنا کرے گا۔ (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریر وقال قال رسول الله له من ادرك الامام جالسا قبل ان يسلم فقد ادرك الصلوة . (دار قطنی ، باب فیمن یدرک من الجمعة رکتہ اولم یدرکھا ، ج ثانی، ص ۱۰ نمبر ۱۵۸۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سلام سے پہلے بھی امام کے ساتھ مل جائے تو گویا کہ اس نے جمعہ پالیا۔ اس لئے اب دو رکعت جمعہ ہی پڑھے گا۔ واللہ اعلم
(813) And whoever catches it (Jumu'ah) in the tashahhud or the prostration of forgetfulness should complete [it as] Jumu'ah. And Allah knows best. Translation: (813) Whoever catches Jumu'ah in the tashahhud or the prostration of forgetfulness should complete it as Jumu'ah. Explanation: Catching Jumu'ah in the tashahhud or sajdat al-sahw means joining the imam before the salam. Then he will complete the prayer as a follower, praying Jumu'ah, not Zuhr. Evidence: (1) This hadith: Abu Hurairah reported that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'When you hear the iqamah, proceed to prayer with calmness and dignity, do not rush. Whatever you catch, pray; and whatever you miss, complete.' (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith indicates that whatever is caught with the imam is prayed, and what is missed is made up. So if one joins before salam, he catches the prayer. (2) Another hadith: Abu Hurairah said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Whoever catches the imam sitting before he says salam has indeed caught the prayer.' (Darqutni). This shows that catching the imam before salam means he has caught Jumu'ah, so he prays two rak'ahs of Jumu'ah.
Source pages p. 80

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with two hadith proofs. The ruling: if a person joins the Jumu'ah prayer when the imam is in the tashahhud (the final sitting) or is performing sajdat al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) - i.e., at any point before the salam - then that person has caught the Jumu'ah prayer. He should complete the prayer as Jumu'ah (two rak'ahs) rather than switching to Zuhr prayer. The key point is that catching the imam before the salam constitutes catching the entire prayer in terms of its identity as Jumu'ah. This is based on the general hadith: 'Whatever you catch, pray; whatever you miss, complete.' The second hadith from Darqutni specifically states that catching the imam sitting (in tashahhud) before salam means catching the prayer. Therefore, the latecomer does not need to pray Zuhr; he prays the remainder as Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The final sitting of the prayer in which the tashahhud supplication is recited.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed before salam to compensate for certain omissions or additions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a person joins the Jumu'ah prayer while the imam is in the tashahhud, what should he do?
A) He should wait and pray Zuhr instead
B) He should complete the prayer as Jumu'ah
C) He must start Jumu'ah from the beginning
D) He should pray two rak'ahs of nafl

Key Takeaway
Catching Jumu'ah before the imam's salam, even in tashahhud, is sufficient to complete the prayer as Jumu'ah according to the Hanafi school.
