The Wajib Status of Eid Prayer
States ruling that Eid prayer is wajib with Quranic proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligation of Eid prayer and identify the Quranic proofs from Surah al-Baqarah and al-Kawthar that establish its wajib status.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib for those with Jumu'ah obligation, proven by the command to pray in Surah al-Kawthar.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on Eid prayer. The text clarifies that the Eid prayer is not merely a sunnah but holds the status of wajib, based on two Quranic verses. It also specifies that this obligation applies to the same people who are obligated for Jumu'ah—resident free men. Understanding this helps the student recognise the weight of this act of worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
The text states that Eid prayer is wajib fi al-ashahh (in the most correct view) for those upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory. This limits the obligation to resident free males; women, travellers, and others are not obligated.
The condition 'upon whom Jumu'ah is wajib' is key.
2
Examine the First Proof: Surah al-Baqarah 2:185
The verse mentions completing the fast and magnifying Allah. According to Tafsir al-Tabari, this refers to the takbir of Eid al-Fitr, thus establishing the occasion and obligation of the Eid prayer.
The proof is indirect; the verse does not directly command the Eid prayer but is interpreted to relate to it.
3
Examine the Second Proof: Surah al-Kawthar 108:2
The imperative 'fashalli' (so pray) is a direct command. In Hanafi usul, a command indicates obligation (wujub). The command to sacrifice after the prayer further supports the sequence and obligation of the Eid al-Adha prayer.
The imperative form is central to the Hanafi argument.
4
Understand the Wajib Category
Wajib in the Hanafi school is a level below fard, established by zanni (probable) evidence. Omission of a wajib act is sinful, but the act is not required to be repeated in its specific form if missed. For Eid prayer, if missed, it is not made up individually.
Compare with fard, which is based on qat'i evidence and must be repeated if missed.
5
Recognize the Cross-Madhhab Difference
Imam al-Shafi'i considers Eid prayer as sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), not wajib. This difference arises from a different interpretation of the Quranic verses and the weight given to other evidence.
The Hanafi position is the relied-upon view (al-ashahh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العيدين

(۸۱۴) صلوة العيد واجبة فى الاصح على من تجب عليه الجمعة

باب : عیدین کے بیان میں

ضروری نوٹ: عید کی نماز واجب ہے۔ زمانہ جاہلیت میں لوگ عید مناتے تھے۔ بعد میں اسلام میں بھی اس کو برقرار رکھا۔ (۱) اس کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہے۔ ولتكملوا العدة ولتكبروا الله على ما هداكم ولعلكم تشكرون (آیت ۱۸۵ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) تفسیر طبری میں ہے کہ اس آیت میں عید الفطر میں تکبیر کہنے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ کیونکہ اسی آیت کے شروع میں روزے کا تذکرہ ہے۔ جس سے عید الفطر کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔ (۲) اور فصل لربک وانحر. ( آیت ۲ ،سورۃ الکوثر ۱۰۸) اس آیت میں تذکرہ ہے کہ پہلے عید الاضحی کی نماز پڑھو پھر جانور کی قربانی کرو۔ اس لئے دونوں آیتوں سے عید الفطر اور عیدالاضحی کا ثبوت ہوتا ہے۔
Chapter of the Two Eids. (814) The Eid prayer is wajib in the most correct opinion for the one upon whom Jumu'ah is obligatory. Chapter: Regarding the two Eids. Essential note: Eid prayer is wajib. In the time of ignorance, people celebrated Eid. Later in Islam, it was maintained. (1) Its proof is from this verse: 'And to complete the number and to magnify Allah for having guided you, and that perhaps you will be thankful' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:185). In Tafsir al-Tabari, it is mentioned that this verse mentions takbir on Eid al-Fitr, because at the beginning of this verse, fasting is mentioned, from which the proof of Eid al-Fitr is established. (2) And 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice' (Surah al-Kawthar 108:2). In this verse, it is mentioned that first pray the Eid al-Adha prayer, then sacrifice an animal. Therefore, from both verses, the proof of Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha is established.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that Eid prayer is wajib (obligatory) for those upon whom Jumu'ah prayer is wajib. It clarifies that the conditions are the same, so men are obliged while women are not. The author indicates this is the most correct opinion (al-ashahh). The proofs are drawn from two Quranic verses: First, Surah al-Baqarah 2:185, which mentions completing the fast and magnifying Allah, interpreted as referring to Eid al-Fitr takbir. Second, Surah al-Kawthar 108:2, which commands prayer and sacrifice, interpreted as referring to Eid al-Adha prayer followed by sacrifice. Both verses together establish the obligation of both Eid prayers.

Key Terms
واجبة (wajibah): In this context, wajib means obligatory, a legal obligation less than fard, omission of which is sinful but does not necessitate complete repetition? Actually, Eid prayer is wajib; if left without excuse, it is sinful.
فى الاصح (fi al-ashahh): Refers to the most correct or relied-upon opinion within the Hanafi school, chosen by later scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Only for those who are not travelling

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib for those with Jumu'ah obligation, established by the imperatives in Surah al-Kawthar and the mention of takbir in Surah al-Baqarah.

Conditions of Eid Prayer: Khutbah Not Required for Validity
States conditions for Eid prayer and explains khutbah is not a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of Eid prayer and explain why the khutbah is not a condition for its validity according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is valid without khutbah, though disliked — a key difference from Jumu'ah.

This passage clarifies the Hanafi position that the khutbah is not a condition (shart) for Eid prayer, contrasting with Jumu'ah. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rulings of the two prayers, especially when a khutbah is omitted or given before the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: Eid prayer is valid without a khutbah, but it is disliked (makruh tanzih) to omit it.
The text uses 'ma'a al-isā'ah' indicating dislike.
2
Compare with Jumu'ah
Note two differences: (1) In Jumu'ah, khutbah precedes prayer; in Eid, it follows. (2) In Jumu'ah, khutbah is a condition; in Eid, it is not.
If Jumu'ah khutbah is omitted, Zuhr must be prayed instead; not so for Eid.
3
Examine the proof
The hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas show the Prophet and caliphs praying Eid before the khutbah. This consistent practice establishes the sunnah sequence and implies khutbah is not a condition.
Dalil is ahad but thubut is qati' (muttafaq alayh).
4
Determine the hukm
Since the khutbah is not a shart, omitting it does not invalidate the prayer. However, it is disliked because it is a sunnah mu'akkadah to deliver it after the prayer.
Dislike here is tanzihi (close to prohibited? Actually karahah tanzihiyyah).

تشریح : جو شرطیں جمعہ قائم کرنے کے لئے ہیں مثلا شہر ہو، قاضی ہو وہی شرطیں عید قائم کرنے کے لئے بھی ہیں ،صرف دو فرق ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ جمعہ میں خطبہ پہلے ہے اور بعد میں نماز ہے، اور عید میں نماز پہلے ہے اور بعد میں خطبہ ہے ، دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ جمعہ میں خطبہ شرط ہے ، اگر خطبہ نہیں پڑھا تو ظہر کی نماز پڑھے ، اور عید میں بغیر خطبہ کے بھی نماز پڑھی تو کراہیت کے ساتھ نماز ہو جائے گی۔

وجه : (۱) نماز کے بعد خطبہ دینے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وابو بكر و عمر يصلون العيدين قبل الخطبة (بخاری شریف ، باب الخطبة بعد العید ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۱۹۶۳ر مسلم شریف، باب کتاب صلاۃ العیدین، ص ۱۳۵۳، نمبر ۲۰۴۴/۸۸۴) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خطبہ نماز کے بعد دیا جائے گا۔ (۲) سمعت ابن عباس قال خرجت مع النبي عل يوم فطر او اضحى فصلى العيد ثم خطب ثم اتى النساء فوعظهن ( بخاری شریف، باب خروج الصبیان الی المصلی ، ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۹۷۵ر مسلم شریف ، باب کتاب صلاۃ العیدین ، ص ۳۵۴، نمبر ۲۰۴۵/۸۸۴) اس حدیث میں خطبے کا تذکرہ ہے،اور یہ بھی ہے کہ نماز کے بعد خطبہ دیا۔
Chapter of the Two Eids. (815) With its conditions except the khutbah, so it is valid without it with dislike, just as if the khutbah is advanced before the Eid prayer. Commentary: The conditions for establishing Jumu'ah, such as being in a city, having a judge, are the same conditions for establishing Eid, with only two differences: [1] In Jumu'ah, the khutbah comes first and then the prayer, while in Eid the prayer comes first and then the khutbah; [2] In Jumu'ah, the khutbah is a condition; if the khutbah is not given, one prays Zuhr instead, while in Eid, even if one prays without the khutbah, the prayer is valid with dislike. Proof: (1) The evidence for delivering the khutbah after the prayer is this hadith: from Ibn Umar: The Prophet (peace be upon him), Abu Bakr, and Umar used to pray the two Eids before the khutbah. (Bukhari, Bab al-Khutbah ba'd al-Eid; Muslim, Kitab Salat al-'Eidayn) From this, it is understood that the khutbah will be given after the prayer. (2) I heard Ibn Abbas say: I went out with the Prophet on the day of Fitr or Adha, and he prayed the Eid prayer, then delivered the khutbah, then went to the women and admonished them. (Bukhari, Bab Khuruj al-Sibyan; Muslim, Kitab Salat al-'Eidayn) In this hadith, the khutbah is mentioned, and also that he gave the khutbah after the prayer.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage clarifies the conditions for Eid prayer. The matn states that Eid prayer has the same conditions as Jumu'ah except for the khutbah. This means that Eid prayer is valid without a khutbah, though it is disliked (makruh) to omit it. The commentary highlights two differences: first, in Jumu'ah the khutbah precedes the prayer, while in Eid it follows; second, in Jumu'ah the khutbah is a condition (shart) for the prayer's validity—if omitted, one must pray Zuhr instead—but in Eid, the khutbah is not a condition, so the prayer remains valid even if the khutbah is omitted or presented before the prayer, albeit with dislike. The proof for the post-prayer khutbah is from the practice of the Prophet and the caliphs as reported by Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas.

Key Terms
بشرائطها (bishara'itiha): Meaning: with its conditions, referring to the conditions of Jumu'ah such as city, ruler, etc.
سوى الخطبة (siwa al-khutbah): Except the khutbah, meaning the khutbah is not a condition for Eid prayer unlike Jumu'ah.
مع الاسائة (ma'a al-isā'ah): With dislike (makruh), meaning although the prayer is valid without khutbah, it is disliked to omit it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The prayer is valid but it is disliked (makruh)
C) The prayer is valid and there is no dislike
D) The prayer is invalid and one must pray Zuhr instead

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is valid without a khutbah, but it is disliked to omit it; this differs from Jumu'ah where the khutbah is a condition.

Proofs for Obligation of Eid Prayer and Its Conditions
Proofs for Eid prayer obligation and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Eid prayer, cite the Quranic and hadith proofs for its obligation, and explain why the khutbah is sunnah rather than a condition.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, supported by Quranic imperative and Prophetic continuity; the khutbah is a separate sunnah after the prayer.

The first part of the passage establishes the ruling that Eid prayer is valid with the same conditions as Jumu'ah, except that the khutbah is not a condition—omitting it is makruh but does not invalidate. The author then presents three proofs for its obligation: the Quranic imperative in Surah al-Kawthar, the Prophet's continuous practice of never leaving the Eid prayer, and his command for women to attend. Understanding these proofs and the distinction between fard and wajib is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the two Eid prayers (Salat al-Eidayn). The ruling is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The proofs cited are: (1) Quran 108:2 (al-Kawthar), (2) Hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing continuous practice, (3) Hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah commanding women to attend.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the verse: The imperative 'salli' indicates obligation per Hanafi usul (al-amr yufidu al-wujub). For the hadith: The Prophet's continuity of practice (istimrar) and never leaving it indicates obligation. The command to women implies obligation for men.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers Eid prayer sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, and may view the khutbah as part of the prayer.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis perform the prayer as wajib and schedule the khutbah after; Shafi'is may consider it sunnah and may have different rules if khutbah is missed.

( بخاری شریف، باب خروج النساء والحيض الی المصلی ، ص ۱۵۶ نمبر ۱۹۷۴ مسلم شریف، باب ذکرا باحته خروج النساء في العيدين الى المصلی ، ص ۱۳۵۵ نمبر ۲۰۵۴/۸۹۰) اس حدیث میں جب عورتوں کو عید کے لئے نکلنے کا حکم دیا تو اس سے پتہ چلتا ہے کہ عید کی نماز واجب ہے۔ ترجمه : (۱۵) جمعہ کی شرائط کے ساتھ سوائے خطبہ کے۔ پس بغیر خطبہ کےعید صیح ہے کراہیت کے ساتھ، جیسے عید کی نماز پر خطبہ مقدم کر دے۔ تشریح : جو شرطیں جمعہ قائم کرنے کے لئے ہیں مثلا شہر ہو، قاضی ہو وہی شرطیں عید قائم کرنے کے لئے بھی ہیں ،صرف دو فرق ہیں [1] ایک یہ کہ جمعہ میں خطبہ پہلے ہے اور بعد میں نماز ہے، اور عید میں نماز پہلے ہے اور بعد میں خطبہ ہے ، دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ جمعہ میں خطبہ شرط ہے ، اگر خطبہ نہیں پڑھا تو ظہر کی نماز پڑھے ، اور عید میں بغیر خطبہ کے بھی نماز پڑھی تو کراہیت کے ساتھ نماز ہو جائے گی۔ وجه : (۱) نماز کے بعد خطبہ دینے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وابو بكر و عمر يصلون العيدين قبل الخطبة (بخاری شریف ، باب الخطبة بعد العید ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۱۹۶۳ر مسلم شریف، باب کتاب صلاۃ العیدین، ص ۱۳۵۳، نمبر ۲۰۴۴/۸۸۴) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خطبہ نماز کے بعد دیا جائے گا۔ (۲) سمعت ابن عباس قال خرجت مع النبي عل يوم فطر او اضحى فصلى العيد ثم خطب ثم اتى النساء فوعظهن ( بخاری شریف، باب خروج الصبیان الی المصلی ، ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۹۷۵ر مسلم شریف ، باب کتاب صلاۃ العیدین ، ص ۳۵۴، نمبر ۲۰۴۵/۸۸۴) اس حدیث میں خطبے کا تذکرہ ہے،اور یہ بھی ہے کہ نماز کے بعد خطبہ دیا۔
Chapter of the Two Eids. (815) With its conditions except the sermon, so it is valid without it with offensiveness, as if the sermon is presented before the Eid prayer. Proof: (1) The proof for the obligation of the two Eid prayers is this verse: 'So pray to your Lord and sacrifice.' (Surah al-Kawthar, 108:2) In this verse, 'pray' is in the imperative form which indicates obligation, so from it is evidence that the Eid prayer is obligatory. (2) The evidence of this hadith: from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to go out on the day of Fitr and Adha to the prayer ground, and the first thing he would begin with was the prayer, then he would turn and stand facing the people while the people were sitting in rows, and he would admonish them, advise them, and command them. (Bukhari, chapter on going out to the prayer ground without a minbar, p.131, no.956) In this hadith, it mentions that he always did this: he would go out for Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha. This continuity and persistence indicates obligation. He never left the two Eid prayers—this is evidence of obligation. (3) In hadith, encouragement for women also to come to the prayer ground: from Umm 'Atiyyah who said: Our Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded us to bring out the secluded women and those in seclusion. (Bukhari, chapter on the exit of women and menstruating women to the prayer ground, p.156, no.1974; Muslim, chapter on mentioning the exit of women for the two Eids to the prayer ground, p.1355, no.2054/890) In this hadith, when women are commanded to go out for Eid, it indicates that the Eid prayer is obligatory. Translation: (15) With the conditions of Jumu'ah except the sermon. Thus without the sermon, the Eid is valid with offensiveness, as if the sermon is presented before the Eid prayer. Explanation: The conditions for establishing Jumu'ah, such as being in a city, having a judge, the same conditions are for establishing Eid. There are only two differences: [1] One is that in Jumu'ah the sermon is first and then the prayer, and in Eid the prayer is first and then the sermon. The second matter is that in Jumu'ah the sermon is a condition; if it is not delivered, one performs Zuhr. And in Eid, if the prayer is performed without the sermon, the prayer is valid with offensiveness. Proof: (1) The proof for delivering the sermon after the prayer is this hadith: from Ibn 'Umar who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him), Abu Bakr, and 'Umar used to pray the two Eids before the sermon. (Bukhari, chapter on the sermon after Eid, p.131, no.1963; Muslim, chapter on the book of the two Eid prayers, p.1353, no.2044/884) From this it is known that the sermon will be given after the prayer. (2) I heard Ibn 'Abbas say: I went out with the Prophet (peace be upon him) on the day of Fitr or Adha, so he prayed the Eid, then delivered the sermon, then came to the women and admonished them. (Bukhari, chapter on the exit of children to the prayer ground, p.132, no.975; Muslim, chapter on the book of the two Eid prayers, p.354, no.2045/884) In this hadith, the sermon is mentioned, and also that he delivered the sermon after the prayer.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the two Eid prayers (Salat al-Eidayn). The matn states that the Eid prayer is valid with the same conditions as Jumu'ah, except that the khutbah (sermon) is not a condition—omitting it renders the prayer valid but makruh (offensive), similar to if the khutbah were presented before the prayer. The commentary then provides proofs for the wajib nature of Eid prayer from the Quran (Surah al-Kawthar, verse 2: the imperative 'pray' indicates wujub according to Hanafi usul) and from Sunnah (the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing the Prophet's continuous practice, and the hadith of Umm 'Atiyyah commanding women to attend, implying obligation). The Hanafi position is that Eid prayer is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni in transmission (ahad hadith and interpretation of the verse). The conditions for Eid are the same as Jumu'ah: being in a city, having a just ruler (or his deputy), public gathering, etc., but the khutbah comes after the prayer. If the khutbah is omitted, the prayer still counts, whereas in Jumu'ah the khutbah is a condition (shart) for validity. The hadith of Ibn 'Umar and Ibn 'Abbas confirm that the khutbah follows the prayer. This is a distinctive Hanafi view; in other schools, the khutbah may be considered part of the prayer or a condition.

Key Terms
عيدين (al-eidayn): The two Eids: Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
خطبة (khutbah): The sermon delivered on the occasion of Eid (or Jumu'ah).
وجوب (wujub): Obligation, a level between fard (definitive) and sunnah (recommended).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh (offensive).
C) The prayer is invalid and one must pray Zuhr instead.
D) The prayer is valid and there is no issue.

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school, supported by Quranic imperative and Prophetic practice; the khutbah is a sunnah performed after the prayer, and omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

Mustahabb Actions on Eid al-Fitr: The Sunnah of Eating an Odd Number of Dates
Enumeration of recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr with hadith for eating dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the thirteen mustahabb actions for Eid al-Fitr and explain the evidence for eating an odd number of dates before the prayer.

Core Idea
Eating an odd number of dates before Eid al-Fitr prayer is sunnah muakkadah, established by the Prophet's continuous practice.

Eid al-Fitr is a day of celebration and gratitude. The Hanafi school lists thirteen recommended actions to enhance the spirit of the day. Among them, eating before the prayer – specifically an odd number of dates – is a confirmed sunnah. This lesson examines these practices and the prophetic proof for the first one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states it is mustahabb to eat on the morning of Eid al-Fitr, and specifically to eat an odd number of dates. The commentary clarifies that this is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Not wajib; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Anas ibn Malik in Bukhari and Tirmidhi: the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten dates, and he would eat them in odd numbers.
The hadith is ahad (single narration) but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's continuous practice (fi'l) of eating dates before the prayer, coupled with the specific odd number, establishes the sunnah. The absence of a verbal command does not lower the status; the action itself indicates recommendation.
In Hanafi usul, a continuous prophetic action indicates sunnah muakkadah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no major ikhtilaf on this point; it is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon). The distinction between Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha (eat after prayer) is notable.
On Eid al-Adha, the sunnah is to eat after the prayer.
5
Evaluate the other mustahabbat
The passage lists twelve additional actions such as ghusl, miswak, perfume, good clothes, etc. All are mustahabb or sunnah, not wajib. The list provides a comprehensive sunnah practice for the day.
Each action has its own evidence, but the passage only provides proof for the eating.

Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage lists thirteen mustahabb (recommended) actions for Eid al-Fitr, as per the Hanafi school. The matn states it is recommended to eat, and specifically to eat an odd number of dates. The commentary elaborates on the first item: it is sunnah (muakkadah) to eat a sweet thing, preferably an odd number of dates, before going to the Eid prayer. The proof is from the hadith of Anas that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not go out on Eid al-Fitr until he had eaten dates, and he would eat an odd number. The other twelve actions include ghusl, miswak, perfume, wearing good clothes, paying Sadaqat al-Fitr before the prayer, expressing joy, giving extra charity, waking up early (tabkir), going early to the prayer ground (ibtikar), praying Fajr in the neighborhood mosque, walking slowly to the prayer ground while reciting takbir, and returning by a different route. These are all considered sunnah or mustahabb, not wajib. For Eid al-Adha, the practice is different: the Prophet would not eat until after the prayer, as indicated by the incomplete sentence at the end.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): A recommended practice established by the Prophet's continuous action; omitting it is not sinful but leaves one deprived of reward.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; similar to sunnah but sometimes used for acts with slightly less emphasis.
وتر (watr): Odd number; here it means eating an odd number of dates (e.g., 3, 5, 7).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the sunnah regarding eating on the morning of Eid al-Fitr according to this passage?
A) It is wajib to eat an odd number of dates before the prayer.
B) It is sunnah to eat a sweet thing, preferably an odd number of dates, before the prayer.
C) It is sunnah to eat after the prayer, especially meat.
D) It is mustahabb to eat only dates, but not necessarily odd.

Key Takeaway
Eating an odd number of dates before the Eid al-Fitr prayer is a confirmed sunnah, supported by the Prophet's practice, and part of a larger set of thirteen mustahabb acts.

Recommended Acts Before Eid al-Fitr Prayer
Lists and proves thirteen recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the thirteen recommended acts for Eid al-Fitr according to the Hanafi school and identify the proofs for each from hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet’s practice on Eid includes eating odd dates, ghusl, and charity before prayer.

This passage from Thamarat al-Najah enumerates the recommended acts (mandubat) for Eid al-Fitr, giving both the list and the scriptural evidence. As a ruling with proof, it shows how Hanafi fiqh derives sunnah practices from the Prophet’s actions and analogies. Understanding these acts helps you prepare for Eid with the proper sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their legal category
Read through the list and classify each act as sunnah muakkadah (most) or wajib (sadaqat al-fitr). Note that the author explicitly states the hukm for each.
The term 'mandub' here is equivalent to sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For each recommended act, find the hadith or qiyas that the author provides. For example, eating dates is proven by Anas's hadith; ghusl by Ibn Abbas; good clothes by Umar's hadith.
Some acts are proven by multiple proofs.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof indicates recommendation (not obligation). For the Prophet's actions (fi'l), the Hanafi principle is that his action indicates sunnah unless there is evidence of obligation.
The hadith uses 'la yaghdu' (he would not go out until…), implying it was his practice.
4
Apply the ruling to a real scenario
Take a specific act, e.g., wearing best clothes. Determine if it is valid to wear new clothes after the prayer if missed before? The sunnah is before prayer, but after is still permissible.
The ruling applies to the timing; missing the sunnah time does not make the act forbidden.
5
Note the exceptional act: sadaqat al-fitr
This is wajib, not sunnah. The author emphasizes it should be paid before the prayer. Understand the difference in legal weight.
If unpaid before prayer, the wajib remains due.

And thirteen things are recommended in al-Fitr: (816) that he eat, and that what is eaten be dates and an odd number. And in Eid al-Fitr, thirteen things are mustahabb: eating an odd number of dates before the prayer, performing ghusl, using miswak, applying perfume, wearing good clothes, paying sadaqat al-fitr if it is obligatory before the Eid prayer, showing happiness, giving extra charity according to one's ability, waking up early (tabkir), going early to the prayer ground (ibtikar), performing Fajr prayer in the local mosque, going to the prayer ground on foot slowly saying takbir, returning by a different route. Translation: (812) [1] It is sunnah that he eat, and that what is eaten be an odd number of dates. Chapter of the Two Eids. Explanation: Since he has been fasting all of Ramadan, now it is sunnah to eat something sweet, and eating an odd number of dates is sunnah. Evidence: (1) It is sunnah to eat something sweet on Eid al-Fitr. For this, there is the hadith: from Anas ibn Malik who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten some dates. And in another hadith: Anas narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he would eat them odd in number. (Bukhari, Book of Eating on the Day of Fitr Before Going Out, p. 130, no. 953; Tirmidhi, Book of Eating on the Day of Fitr Before Going Out, p. 142, no. 542) From the hadith, it is known that before going to the prayer ground on Eid al-Fitr, one should eat something sweet. And on Eid al-Adha, after the prayer... (page 84) ...eating is recommended. (2) In this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Buraidah from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten, and would not eat on the day of Nahr until he had sacrificed. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Leaving Eating on the Day of Nahr Until Sacrificing, vol. 3, p. 401, no. 6159; Tirmidhi, Book of Eating on the Day of Fitr Before Going Out, p. 142, no. 542) (3) From Abdullah ibn Buraidah from his father who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten, and would not eat on the day of Adha until he had prayed. (Tirmidhi, Book of Eating on the Day of Fitr Before Going Out, p. 142, no. 542?; Ibn Majah, Book of Eating on the Day of Fitr Before Going Out, p. 250, no. 1756) In this hadith, it is that he would eat before the prayer on Eid al-Fitr and after the prayer on Eid al-Adha. Translation: (817) [2] Performing ghusl. [3] Using miswak. [4] Applying perfume. [5] Wearing good clothes. These are sunnah. Explanation: Performing ghusl, using miswak, applying perfume, and wearing good clothes on the two Eids are sunnah. Evidence: (1) This is a gathering and a day of happiness, so all these things are sunnah. (2) Ghusl is sunnah. For this, there is the hadith: from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah would perform ghusl on the day of Fitr and the day of Adha. (Ibn Majah, Book of Ghusl on the Two Eids, p. 186, no. 1315) (3) From Ibn Umar that he would perform ghusl on the two Eids like ghusl from janabah. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Book of Ghusl for the Eids, vol. 1, p. 447, no. 1428; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 550, no. 5770) (4) Eid is like Jumu'ah, so whatever is sunnah in Jumu'ah is sunnah in Eid. And in Jumu'ah, these things are sunnah. From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever performs ghusl on Friday and wears his best clothes and applies perfume if he has it, then comes to Jumu'ah. (Abu Dawud, Book of Ghusl for Jumu'ah, p. 56, no. 343) From this hadith, it is known that on Friday, one should perform ghusl, wear good clothes, and apply perfume. (5) The hadith for wearing good clothes is: that Abdullah ibn Umar said: Umar took a cloak of istabraq that was being sold in the market, took it, and came to the Messenger of Allah and said: O Messenger of Allah, buy this and adorn yourself with it for the Eid and for delegations. (Bukhari, Book of the Two Eids and Adornment therein, p. 130, no. 948) In this hadith, 'adorn yourself with it for the Eid and for delegations' indicates that wearing good clothes and looking handsome for Eid is sunnah. Translation: (818) [2] Pay sadaqat al-fitr if it is obligatory. Explanation: It is better to pay sadaqat al-fitr before going to the prayer ground, and if one could not, the obligation does not drop; rather, one must pay it later. Evidence: from Ibn Umar who said: The Messenger of Allah made obligatory zakat al-fitr, one sa' of dates or one sa' of barley, upon the slave and the free, the male and the female, the young and the old from the Muslims, and he ordered that it be paid before the people go out to the prayer.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a detailed listing of the recommended acts (mustahabbat) for Eid al-Fitr, with proofs from hadith. The author first enumerates thirteen acts in summary form, then explains each with evidence. The first act is eating before the Eid prayer, preferably an odd number of dates. The author cites multiple hadith showing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would eat dates before the Fitr prayer and not eat before the Adha prayer until after. The second set includes ghusl, miswak, perfume, and good clothes, proven by hadith and analogy with Jumu'ah. The next is paying sadaqat al-fitr before the prayer, which is wajib and should be paid early. The author quotes Ibn Umar's hadith on the obligation of sadaqat al-fitr. The commentary shows that these acts are sunnah or mustahabb based on direct prophetic practice and general principles. The Hanafi position is that all these are sunnah (or mustahabb) except sadaqat al-fitr which is wajib. The passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of using hadith and qiyas to establish recommended acts.

Key Terms
مندوب (mandub): Recommended act; synonymous with mustahabb, sunnah ghayr muakkadah or muakkadah depending on context.
وترا (witr): Odd number; here specifically eating an odd number of dates (e.g., 1, 3, 5).
صدقۃ الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): Obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, before Eid prayer, per head of household.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The Prophet's sunnah for Eid includes specific acts of worship and preparation; following them brings reward and aligns with his practice.

Sunan Acts Before Eid Prayer in the Hanafi School
Lists and proves sunan acts before Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunan acts before Eid prayer and explain the Hanafi evidence from hadith and qiyas with Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
Four sunan acts before Eid are sunnah muakkadah, proven by hadith and analogy with Jumu'ah.

In this passage, the author lists four recommended actions before the Eid prayer and provides their proofs. Understanding these rulings helps you distinguish between sunnah and wajib in the Hanafi school and appreciate how the school uses multiple sources of evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and ruling level
List the four acts: ghusl, miswak, perfume, best clothes. Note that the text explicitly calls them 'sunnah' (sunnah hain). In Hanafi terminology, this means sunnah muakkadah unless stated otherwise.
These are sunnah, not wajib. Neglecting them does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Locate the direct hadith for ghusl
Find the hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet used to perform ghusl on Eid. In Hanafi usul, a regular action of the Prophet without a command indicates sunnah, not wajib.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which lowers the level of obligation.
3
Analyze the qiyas with Jumu'ah
The author argues that Eid is like Jumu'ah in being a congregational gathering, so what is sunnah for Jumu'ah is sunnah for Eid. This is a valid qiyas in the Hanafi school because the illa (effective cause) is the gathering.
Proof for Jumu'ah sunnan comes from the hadith of Abu Sa'id and Abu Hurairah.
4
Identify the proof for best clothes
The hadith of Umar buying a fine garment and the Prophet's approval shows that wearing best clothes for Eid is a sunnah. The phrase 'li al-'eid' directly links the action to Eid.
Perfume and miswak are included by analogy with Jumu'ah and general practice.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
All four acts are sunnah muakkadah based on direct hadith for ghusl, qiyas with Jumu'ah for all, and a specific hadith for clothes. The passage does not mention any intra-Hanafi disagreement.
The ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof statement about the sunnan acts before the Eid prayer. The author lists four actions: ghusl, miswak, applying perfume, and wearing best clothes. These are classified as sunnah, not wajib. The reasoning includes: (1) analogical reasoning (qiyas) with Jumu'ah, since both are congregational gatherings; (2) direct hadith evidence for ghusl on Eid from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar; (3) a hadith from Abu Sa'id and Abu Hurairah about Jumu'ah ghusl, perfume, and best clothes, applied by analogy to Eid; (4) a specific hadith about Umar buying a fine garment for Eid and receiving delegations. The passage also includes an unrelated note about eating on Eid (mustahab) and a hadith about the timing of eating, which is likely an additional benefit. The overall ruling is clear: these four acts are sunnah muakkadah, following the Hanafi position.

Showing Happiness on Eid
Ruling and proof for displaying joy on Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on expressing joy on Eid and explain how the hadith of Aisha serves as proof.

Core Idea
Showing permissible happiness on Eid is a sunnah, as the Prophet approved celebration.

Eid is a day of joy and community. The Hanafi school teaches that displaying happiness, within lawful boundaries, is not merely allowed but recommended. This lesson examines a famous hadith where the Prophet explicitly defended the expression of joy, setting a precedent for how Muslims should celebrate their festivals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the precise act being ruled upon — showing happiness and cheerfulness on Eid. Note that the ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
The source says 'khushi wa khurmi zahir karna' - showing happiness. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's action and words.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Read the hadith of Aisha carefully. The Prophet's statement 'Every nation has a festival, and this is our festival' is the key evidence.
The hadith is from Bukhari, making it sound (sahih) but ahad (single-chain) in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how it proves)
Understand the connection: the Prophet allowed singing and did not rebuke Abu Bakr's initial objection; instead, he taught that Eid has its own spirit, which includes joy and merriment.
The ruling is not explicit in the hadith text but derived from the Prophet's approval (taqrir) and his statement.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi position
Confirm that the Hanafi school consistently encourages joy on Eid, as long as no haram act is involved. This is an act of ibadah in the sense of celebrating Allah's blessing.
Some other schools may be more restrictive, but the Hanafi position is moderate.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling that showing happiness and cheerfulness on Eid is a sunnah. The proof is the famous hadith of Aisha where the Prophet allowed singing by young girls on Eid, despite Abu Bakr's objection, saying 'Every nation has a festival, and this is our festival.' This indicates that expressions of joy, including permissible forms of entertainment, are part of the celebration. The Hanafi school holds that moderate expressions of happiness, such as festive gatherings, wearing nice clothes, and allowing permissible entertainment, are recommended (mustahab) on Eid, as long as no haram acts are committed.

Eid Sunnah: Tabkir, Ibtikar, and Fajr in Local Mosque
Rulings on waking early and proceeding early to the Eid prayer ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunnah acts of Eid morning according to the Hanafi school and explain their evidentiary basis from the hadith and companion practice.

Core Idea
Finish Eid prayer early: wake early, pray Fajr locally, and hasten to the musalla.

This lesson covers three sunnah practices that the Hanafi school recommends for the day of Eid: waking early (tabkir), going early to the prayer ground (ibtikar), and praying Fajr in one's local mosque rather than at the prayer ground. These rulings are derived from authentic hadith and the practice of the companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunnan rulings
Read the passage and list the three recommended actions: tabkir, ibtikar, and praying Fajr in the local mosque. Note that each is labeled 'sunnah'.
2
Examine the first proof: hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr
Read the hadith and note the key point: the companions finished the Eid prayer by the time of tasbih (ishraq). This shows the virtue of early completion.
3
Derive the ruling from the hadith
The hadith implies that it is sunnah to finish the Eid prayer early, which is achieved by going early (ibtikar) and starting on time. The companion's disapproval of delay reinforces this.
4
Examine the second proof: practice of Ibn Umar
Ibn Umar used to pray Fajr in the Prophet's mosque and then proceed directly to the Eid prayer ground. This supports the sunnah of praying Fajr locally and then hastening to the Eid ground.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi school holds these three actions as sunnah muakkadah. There is no known ikhtilaf among the early Hanafi authorities on this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Translation of (821): [9] Tabkir: waking early in the morning. [10] Ibtikar: hastening to the prayer ground. [11] He prays Fajr in his local mosque. Explanation: Waking up early on Eid is sunnah. Hastening to the prayer ground is also sunnah. Praying Fajr in his local mosque is also sunnah. Reasoning: (1) Abdullah ibn Busr, a companion of the Messenger of Allah, went out with the people on a day of Fitr or Adha and disapproved of the imam's delay, saying: 'We used to finish at this time of ours, and that was at the time of tasbih.' (Abu Dawud and Bukhari). In this hadith, 'tasbih' refers to the ishraq prayer, i.e., they would finish the Eid prayer at the time of ishraq. (2) There is also the practice of a companion: Ibn Umar used to pray Fajr in the mosque of the Messenger of Allah, then go out as he was to the prayer ground. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah).
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage covers three sunnan practices related to the timing of Eid: (1) Tabkir: waking up early in the morning on Eid day. (2) Ibtikar: proceeding early to the Eid prayer ground. (3) Praying Fajr in one's local mosque rather than the Eid prayer ground. The text provides two proofs: first, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr, who criticized the imam for delaying and mentioned that the companions used to finish the Eid prayer by the time of ishraq (which is after sunrise). This shows the virtue of performing the Eid prayer early. Second, the practice of Ibn Umar: he would pray Fajr in the Prophet's mosque and then proceed directly to the Eid prayer ground without returning home. The Hanafi school considers these acts sunnah muakkadah to ensure one does not miss the preferred time for the Eid prayer and to avoid unnecessary delay.

Key Terms
تبکیر (tabkir): Waking up early in the morning on Eid day
ابتکار (ibtikar): Hastening to go to the Eid prayer ground early
تسبیح (tasbih): In this context, the time of ishraq prayer (after sunrise)

Rulings on Walking to the Musalla and Reciting Takbir
Ruling on going to the Eid musalla and reciting takbir quietly

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting takbir while walking to the Eid musalla, explain the two narrations regarding when to stop, and identify the evidence (dalil) that supports quiet recitation for Eid al-Fitr.

Core Idea
For Eid al-Fitr, recite takbir quietly on the way; stop upon arrival at the musalla.

The Eid prayer begins with a walk to the musalla, a spacious prayer ground outside the mosque. The Hanafi school provides specific guidance on how and when to recite takbir during this walk. This lesson examines the matn, two internal narrations, and the evidence from Quran and hadith, clarifying the Hanafi approach and distinguishing it from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the text addresses the act of walking to the musalla for Eid prayer and the sunnah of reciting takbir quietly (sirran).
The hukm level is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Note the two riwayat on when to stop
The text presents two narrations: stopping upon reaching the musalla (first riwaya) and stopping when the imam begins the prayer (second riwaya).
The mufta bihi is the first riwaya.
3
Examine the dalil
The Quran verses (7:55, 7:205) emphasize hidden dhikr, and the hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet's practice of stopping at the musalla.
This dalil supports quiet recitation and the first riwaya.
4
Understand intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and tarjih
The two riwayat represent differences within the school; later authorities like al-Marghinani preferred stopping at the musalla.
Tarjih is based on salaf practice and consistency.
5
Compare cross-madhhab differences
Shafi'is and Malikis generally recommend loud takbir for both Eids, while Hanafis differentiate (quiet for Fitr, loud for Adha).
The thamarah al-khilaf is in the audible mode of worship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العيدين (۸۲۲) ثم يتوجه إلى المصلى ماشيا مكبرا سرًا قيقطعه إذا انتهى إلى المصلى في رواية وفي رواية إلى العبدایۃ ساعتۃ. وجه: ادعوا ربكم تضرعا و خفية إنه لا يحب المعتدين (الأعراف 55). أذكر ربك في نفسك تضرعا وخيفة ودون الجهر من القول بالغدو والآصال ولا تكن من الغافلين (الأعراف 205). عن شعبة قال كنت أقود ابن عباس يوم العيد فيسمع الناس يكبرون فقال ما شأن الناس؟ قلت يكبرون قال يكبرون؟ قال يكبر الإمام؟ قلت لا قال أمجانين الناس؟ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة 413 في التكبير إذا خرج إلى العيد). إن عبد الله بن عمر أخبره أن رسول الله كان يكبر يوم الفطر من حين يخرج من بيته حتى يأتي المصلى (دار قطني، كتاب العيدين، ج ثاني، ص134، نمبر 298; مستدرك الحاكم، كتاب صلاة العيدين، ج اول، ص438، نمبر 1105). عن ابن عمر أنه إذا غدا يوم الأضحى ويوم الفطر يجهر بالتكبير حتى يأتي المصلى، ثم يكبر حتى يأتي الإمام (دار قطني، كتاب العيدين، ج ثاني، ص34، نمبر 1700; مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، باب التكبير إذا خرج إلى العيد، ج اول، ص287، نمبر 5618).
Chapter of the Two Eids. (822) Then he proceeds to the musalla walking, reciting takbir quietly, and he stops it when he reaches the musalla in one narration, and in another narration until the beginning of the prayer. Evidence: 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately; indeed, He does not love transgressors.' (Quran 7:55) 'And remember your Lord within yourself in humility and in fear without being apparent in speech - in the mornings and the evenings, and do not be among the heedless.' (Quran 7:205) From Shu'bah: I was leading Ibn Abbas on the day of Eid, and he heard the people reciting takbir. He said, 'What is wrong with the people?' I said, 'They are reciting takbir.' He said, 'They are reciting takbir? Is the imam reciting takbir?' I said, 'No.' He said, 'Are the people insane?' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah) 'Abdullah ibn Umar informed him that the Messenger of Allah used to recite takbir on the day of Fitr from when he left his house until he came to the musalla.' (Dar Qutni; Mustadrak al-Hakim) From Ibn Umar: 'When he went out on the day of Adha and the day of Fitr, he would recite takbir loudly until he came to the musalla, then he would recite takbir until the imam came.' (Dar Qutni; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah)
Source pages p. 86

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) on the way to the Eid prayer. The matn states that one walks to the musalla (Eid prayer ground) while reciting takbir quietly (sirran). Two narrations are given about when to stop: one says upon reaching the musalla, another says until the imam begins the prayer. The commentator provides evidence (wajh) from Quran and hadith. First, Quran verses (7:55 and 7:205) emphasize private, gentle dhikr, supporting silent takbir. Second, a hadith from Ibn Abbas (via Shu'bah) criticizes loud takbir when the imam is not doing it, indicating dislike of unnecessary noise. Third, a hadith from Ibn Umar confirms takbir from leaving home until arriving at the musalla. Fourth, another narration from Ibn Umar adds that takbir continues until the imam arrives. The Hanafi position prefers quiet takbir for Fitr but loud for Adha based on other proofs. The two narrations (riwayat) represent differences within the school; the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is to stop takbir upon reaching the musalla, as it marks the beginning of the prayer gathering.

Key Terms
مصلى (musalla): The place designated for Eid prayer, usually a large open area outside the mosque.
تکبیر (takbir): The phrase 'Allahu Akbar' recited on the way to Eid prayer and at other occasions.
سرا (sirran): Quietly, in a low voice, so as not to disturb others or be ostentatious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When the sun reaches its zenith

D) After completing the Eid prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school instructs quiet takbir for Eid al-Fitr, stopping upon arrival at the musalla, based on prophetic practice and Quranic emphasis on hidden dhikr.

Returning from the Musalla by a Different Route
Ruling on returning from Eid prayer via a different path

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on returning from the Eid musalla by a different route, identify the proof from the Sunnah, and explain the wisdom behind this practice.

Core Idea
Taking a different route home from the Eid prayer is a sunnah muakkadah, following the Prophet's example.

In this lesson, we examine a simple yet meaningful act of worship associated with the Eid prayer. The Hanafi school teaches that it is recommended (sunnah) to return from the musalla by a different path than the one used to go. This practice is based on the authentic hadith of Jabir and carries multiple benefits. Let's explore the ruling, its evidence, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (fard, sunnah, etc.)?
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? Which hadith and from which sources?
The matn cites Jabir's hadith from Bukhari and Abu Dawood.
3

How does the hadith prove the ruling? Which phrase indicates recommendation?
The word 'khalafa' shows a deliberate, habitual action, implying sunnah.
4

Is there any disagreement among schools?
All major schools agree on the recommendation; it is muttafaq alayh.
5
Evaluate the ruling
Why is it sunnah muakkadah and not wajib?
The hadith shows continuous practice but no explicit command, and Hanafi usul classifies such actions as sunnah.

Source Text

(۸۲۳) ويرجع من طريق آخر. وجه: عن جابر قال كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان يوم عيد خالف الطريق (بخاري شريف، باب من خالف الطريق إذا رجع يوم العيد، ص 158، نمبر 986; ابو داود شريف، باب الخروج إلى العيد في طريق ويرجع في طريق، ص 173، نمبر 1156).

The wisdom behind this includes greeting more people, spreading joy, making du'a for more communities, and manifesting the signs of Islam. Hanafis consider this a sunnah (recommended practice) based on this authentic hadith. The matn simply states the ruling; the commentator adds the evidence from Bukhari and Abu Dawood.

Dislike of Nafl Prayer Before and After Eid Prayer
Ruling on disliked nafl prayers around Eid prayer with location distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl prayers before and after Eid prayer and identify the location-based distinction using the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Nafl before Eid is disliked everywhere; after Eid only in the musalla — at home it is permissible.

The Hanafi school draws a precise distinction regarding voluntary prayers on Eid day: while nafl before the Eid prayer is disliked both at the musalla and at home, nafl after the Eid prayer is only disliked at the musalla. This ruling, based on the Prophet's practice, is often misunderstood as a blanket prohibition. In this lesson, we will examine the textual evidence and the reasoning behind the location-based difference.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the act (nafl prayer) and its hukm level (makruh tanzihi) before and after Eid prayer.
2
Identify the location distinction
Note that nafl before Eid is disliked both in the musalla and at home; nafl after Eid is disliked only in the musalla. At home after Eid it is permissible (mubah) or even recommended.
3
Locate the primary dalil
Cite the hadith of Ibn Abbas: the Prophet did not pray nafl before or after the two Eid rak'ahs at the musalla.
Reference: Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawood
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'lam yusalli qablaha wa la ba'daha' indicates deliberate omission, implying dislike. The presence of Bilal confirms this as a public occasion.
5
Note the hadith from Abu Sa'id
The Prophet did not pray before Eid, but upon returning home he prayed two rak'ahs. This shows the location-based exemption.
Reference: Ibn Majah

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۲۴) ويكره التنفل قبل صلوة العيد في المصلى والبيت وبعدها في المصلى فقط على اختيار الجمهور. وجه: عن ابن عباس أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خرج يوم الفطر فصلى ركعتين لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها ومعه بلال (بخاري شريف، باب الصلاة قبل العيد وبعدها، ص135، نمبر 1989; مسلم شريف، باب ترك الصلاة قبل العيد وبعدها في المصلى، ص356، نمبر 1884; ابو داؤد شريف، باب الصلاة بعد صلاة العيد، ص173، نمبر 1159). عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال: كان رسول الله لا يصلي قبل العيد شيئا فإذا رجع إلى منزله صلى ركعتين (ابن ماجه شريف، باب ما جاء في الصلاة قبل صلاة العيد وبعدها، ص183، نمبر 1393). عن ابن عباس كره الصلاة قبل العيد (بخاري شريف، باب الصلاة قبل العيد وبعدها، ص135، نمبر 989).
(824) It is disliked to perform voluntary prayer before Eid prayer in the musalla and at home, and after it only in the musalla, according to the choice of the majority. Evidence: From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet went out on the day of Fitr, prayed two rak'ahs, and did not pray before or after them, with Bilal beside him. (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawood) From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: The Messenger of Allah would not pray anything before the Eid, but when he returned to his home, he would pray two rak'ahs. (Ibn Majah) From Ibn Abbas: He disliked prayer before the Eid. (Bukhari)
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage clarifies the Hanafi ruling on nafl (voluntary) prayers in connection with Eid prayer. The matn states it is makruh (disliked) to pray nafl before Eid prayer both in the musalla and at home, and after Eid prayer only in the musalla (i.e., nafl after Eid at home is not disliked). This is the position chosen by the majority (al-jumhur) of Hanafi scholars. The evidence comes from several hadith: First, Ibn Abbas reports that the Prophet prayed only the two Eid rak'ahs without any nafl before or after, while at the musalla. Second, Abu Sa'id al-Khudri confirms that the Prophet did not pray before Eid, but upon returning home, he would pray two rak'ahs. Third, Ibn Abbas himself expressed dislike for prayer before Eid. These indicate that the prohibition is specifically for the musalla; at home, nafl after Eid is allowed and even practiced by the Prophet. The wisdom is to avoid delay and to mark the difference from regular Friday prayer, where nafl is recommended. Hanafis consider this ruling as makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) based on the Prophet's omission, but not haram.

Key Terms
تنفل (tanafful): Performing voluntary (nafl) prayers beyond the obligatory ones.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act whose avoidance is recommended but not sinful. In this context, makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked).
الجمهور (al-jumhur): The majority of Hanafi scholars (the later authorities who adopted this ruling).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where is it disliked to pray nafl after the Eid prayer?
A) Only in the musalla
B) At home
C) Both in the musalla and at home
D) Neither; it is always permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on nafl around Eid prayer is location-dependent: disliking it at the musalla both before and after, but permitting it at home after Eid.

The Valid Time for Eid Prayer
Definition of the valid time for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid time for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify its beginning and end based on the legal definition.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is valid only from sunrise by a spear's length until the sun's zenith.

The Eid prayer is a special congregational prayer performed on the two Eids. Unlike the five daily prayers, it has a specific time window defined by the position of the sun. This lesson unpacks that definition, explains the measure 'spear's height', and clarifies the evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Eid prayer (salat al-Eid). The Hanafi school considers it sunnah muakkadah, meaning it is highly recommended but not obligatory. The passage does not discuss the ruling explicitly, but it is known from other sources.
The ruling is not derived from this passage alone.
2
Define the time window
The matn states: 'from the rising of a spear (height) until zawal (midday).' This gives both the start and end boundaries.
Zawal is the moment the sun begins to decline from its highest point.
3
Understand the measurement 'spear's height'
One spear's height (irtifa' ramh) is approximately 5-6 feet above the horizon, corresponding to about 15-20 minutes after sunrise. This is a celestial marker used to avoid the prohibited time for prayer at sunrise.
Some schools use two spear heights; Hanafis use one.
4
Identify the evidence
The author cites a hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Anbasah al-Sulami, which establishes this time window. The full hadith is not quoted, but it is the basis for the ruling.
The hadith is a proof (dalil) for the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۸۲۵) ووقت صحة صلوة العيد من ارتفاع رمح إلى الزوال. وجه: عن عمرو بن عنبسة السلمي (الحديث).
(825) And the time for the validity of the Eid prayer is from the rising of a spear (height) until midday (zawal). Evidence: From 'Amr ibn 'Anbasah al-Sulami (the hadith).
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage defines the time window for performing the Eid prayer. The matn states it begins when the sun is 'irtifa' ramh' (the height of a spear) above the horizon, and ends at zawal (when the sun crosses the meridian). A spear's height is estimated at about 5-10 feet above the horizon, corresponding roughly to 15-20 minutes after sunrise. This means Eid prayer should not be performed at sunrise (which is the time for nafl prayer) nor at midday when prayer is generally prohibited. The evidence is from a hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Anbasah (though not quoted fully here), which sets the time for Eid prayer similar to that of the Duha (forenoon) prayer after sunrise by a spear's length. Hanafis consider this time as mustahabb (recommended) to pray early, but the prayer is valid even close to midday as long as it is before zawal. The commentator explains the spear measurement: one spear is about 5 feet, two spears 10 feet, thus the time starts when the sun is 5-10 feet above the horizon, i.e., shortly after sunrise (about 5 minutes after sunrise for ishraq time). However, the preferred practice is to delay a bit to ensure the sun is well above the horizon. This ruling applies to both Eids (Fitr and Adha).

Key Terms
ارتفاع رمح (irtifa' ramh): The height of a spear above the horizon. Typically, one spear length is about 5-6 feet, meaning the sun is well clear of the horizon and brightness is full.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun crosses the meridian and begins to decline; the start of the zuhr prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What marks the end of the valid time for Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sun reaching its zenith (zawal)
B) Sun setting
C) Asr prayer time
D) Mid-afternoon

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is valid only from sunrise by a spear's height until the sun's zenith; this time window ensures the prayer is performed outside prohibited times.

The Sunnah of Taking a Different Route for Eid Prayer
Ruling on sunnah route for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah practice of going to and returning from the Eid prayer and cite the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Go to Eid by one route, return by another—a sunnah that multiplies witnesses and blessings.

The Prophet ﷺ would take different routes to and from the Eid prayer, a practice that is a sunnah mu'akkadah. This lesson covers the evidence and underlying wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah act

2
Locate the primary dalil
The author references a hadith from Abu Dawud. The specific hadith is: 'The Prophet ﷺ would go to the Eid prayer by one route and return by another.' This is a proven sunnah.
The hadith is cited in the commentary after the main text.

Understand the wisdom
Scholars mention wisdom behind this practice: to increase the number of routes that will bear witness on the Day of Judgment, to greet more people, and to manifest the celebrations of Eid.
This wisdom is derived from general Islamic principles.

Ruling on Nafl Prayers Before and After Eid Prayer
Ruling with proof on nafl prohibition for Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl prayers before and after the Eid prayer and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Nafl before Eid is disliked everywhere; after Eid, disliked only in the musalla, not at home.

This lesson details the prohibition of supererogatory prayers before the Eid prayer and the restriction after it. The Hanafi school, following the majority, holds that nafl before Eid is makruh tanzih in all locations, while after Eid it is only makruh in the musalla. The evidence includes multiple hadith and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The text clearly states: 'It is disliked to pray nafl before the Eid prayer in the musalla and at home, and after it only in the musalla.' Understand the distinction: before Eid, it is disliked everywhere; after Eid, only in the musalla.
The Hanafi term is makruh tanzih, meaning it is better to avoid but not sinful.
2
Examine the first proof (rational)
The author gives a rational reason: engaging in nafl would delay the Eid prayer, which should be prioritized. This is a practical wisdom.
3
Examine the second proof (hadith of Ibn Abbas)
The hadith states that the Prophet ﷺ did not pray before or after the Eid prayer. This shows the general prohibition.
This hadith is from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
4
Examine the third proof (hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri)
This hadith shows that the Prophet ﷺ would not pray before Eid, but when he returned home, he prayed two rak'ahs. This permits nafl at home after Eid.
Reported by Ibn Majah.
5
Examine the saying of Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas explicitly disliked prayer before Eid. This supports the dislike for before Eid.
From Bukhari.

Source Text

صلى الله
ابن عباس ان النبي لا خرج يوم الفطر فصلى ركعتين لم يصل قبلها ولا بعدها ومعه بلال . (بخاری شریف باب الصلوۃ قبل العيد و بعدها، ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۱۹۸۹ مسلم شریف ، باب ترک الصلاة قبل العيد و بعدها فی المصلی ، ص ۳۵۶، نمبر ۱۸۸۴ ۲۰۵۷ را بو داؤد شریف، باب الصلوۃ بعد صلوۃ العیدص اے انمبر (۱۱۵۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید کے پہلے اور بعد میں بھی نماز نفل نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ عید گاہ میں نہ پڑھے ، گھر میں پڑھے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عـــن ابـــی سـعـيـد الخدري قال : كان رسول الله الله الله لا يصلى قبل العيد شيئا فاذا رجع الى منزله صلی رکعتین ۔ (ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الصلاة قبل صلاة العيد و بعدھا، ص ۱۸۳ نمبر ۱۳۹۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عید کے بعد گھر میں نفل پڑھ سکتا ہے ۔(۳) قول صحابی میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس كره الصلوة قبل العيد. (بخاری شریف، باب الصلوۃ قبل العيد و بعدهاص ۱۳۵ نمبر ۹۸۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عید سے پہلے تو نفل مکروہ ہے بعد میں نہیں۔
Chapter of the Two Eids. (823) He should open the prayer and return by another route. (824) It is disliked to pray supererogatory prayers before the Eid prayer in the musalla and at home, and after it only in the musalla according to the choice of the majority. (825) The time for the validity of the Eid prayer is from when the sun has risen...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the etiquette of the Eid prayer and the prohibition of supererogatory prayers before and after it. The author states that it is sunnah to go to the Eid prayer by one route and return by another, based on a hadith from Abu Dawud. Then he discusses the ruling on nafl prayers: it is makruh (disliked) to pray nafl before the Eid prayer both in the musalla and at home, and after the Eid prayer only in the musalla; at home it is not makruh. This is the view of the majority (jumhur). The proofs include: (1) rational: preoccupying oneself with nafl would delay the Eid prayer, which should be prioritized; (2) hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not pray before or after the Eid prayer; (3) hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not pray before Eid but when he returned home he prayed two rak'ahs; (4) the saying of Ibn Abbas that he disliked prayer before Eid. Thus, the dislike applies to nafl before Eid everywhere, and after Eid only in the musalla, not at home.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked but not sinful; leaving it is rewarded but doing it is not punished.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory voluntary prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
عیدگاہ (musalla): The open prayer ground designated for Eid prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where is it permissible to pray nafl after the Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) In the musalla only
B) At home only
C) Both in musalla and home
D) Not permissible anywhere

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayers before Eid are makruh everywhere; after Eid, they are makruh only in the musalla, permissible at home.

Time for Eid Prayer
Definition of the valid time for Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time for Eid prayer and identify the hadith evidence that establishes its beginning and end.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time begins when the sun rises one to two spears high and ends at zawal.

When exactly should the Eid prayer be offered? This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the valid time for the two Eid prayers. The author provides a clear definition — from ishraq (when the sun is a spear's height) until the sun's zenith — and supports it with four prophetic hadith. Understanding this time window is essential for correctly performing the wajib Eid prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the time for the Eid prayer, which is wajib according to the Hanafi school. Determine the exact boundaries: beginning and end.
The prayer is not valid before ishraq or after zawal.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites multiple hadith. The first is from 'Amr ibn 'Anbasah (Abu Dawud, Nasa'i) that the Prophet forbade prayer at sunrise until it rises one or two spears — this indicates the start of permissible time.
Other hadith corroborate: the action of 'Abdullah ibn Busr (Eid at ishraq) and the hadith of al-Bara' (prayer before sermon).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase in the hadith is "حتى تطلع الشمس فترتفع قيس رمح أو رمحين" — the command to wait until the sun rises a spear's length shows that prayer at that moment becomes permissible. The prohibition before that is removed.
The specific measure (ramh) indicates a visible height, approximately 5–10 feet above the horizon.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools allow Eid prayer earlier (before ishraq) or later (after zawal). The Hanafi school restricts it strictly to this window, based on the hadith evidence.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue; the practical consequence is the exact timing for Eid congregations.
5
Synthesize the ruling
Combine the proofs: the time for Eid prayer is from ishraq (when the sun is one to two spears high) until zawal (sun at zenith). This is the mufta bihi position.
The derived ruling is that Eid prayer must be performed in the forenoon, after sunrise and before midday.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشمس قدر رمح او رمحين الى زوالها (۸۲۶) وكيفية صلوتهما ان ينوى صلوة العيد ثم يكبر للتحريمة ثم يقرأ الثناء ثم يكبر تكبيرات الزوائد ثلاثا يرفع يديه في كل منها أنه قال قلت يا رسول الله ! أى الليل اسمع ؟ . .. حتى تصلى الصبح ثم اقصر حتى تطلع الشمس فترتفع قيس رمح أو رمحين فانها تطلع بين قرنی شیطان و يصلى لها الكفار ، ثم صل ما شئت فان الصلاة مشهودة مكتوبة حتى يعدل الرمح ظله ثم اقصر فان جهنم تسجر و تفتح ابوابها (ابوداود شریف، باب من رخص فیھما اذا كانت الشمس مرتفعة ، ص۱۹۱، نمبر ۱۲۷۷) (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک نیزہ بلند ہو تو نماز جائز ہے۔ سمعت عمر وبن عبسة يقول .... فدع الصلاة حتى ترتفع قيد رمح ويذهب شعاعها ثم الصلاة محضورة مشهودة حتى تعتدل الشمس اعتدال الرمح بنصف النهار ( نسائی شریف، باب النھی عن الصلوۃ بعد العصر ص ۷۹، نمبر ۵۷۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سورج ایک نیزہ تک بلند ہو جائے تو نماز حلال ہے اور زوال تک حلال رہے گا، یہی عید کی نماز کا وقت ہے۔ (۳) صلى الله قال خرج عبد الله بن بسر صاحب رسول الله له مع الناس في يوم عيد الفطر او اضحی فانكر ابطاء الامام فقال انا كنا قد فرغنا ساعتنا هذه وذلك حين التسبيح (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب وقت الخروج الی العید ص ۱۶۸ نمبر ۱۱۳۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ تسبیح یعنی اشراق کے وقت عید کی نماز پڑھے (۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلے عید کی نماز پڑھی جائے گی۔ عن البراء بن عازب قال قال سمعت النبى عال للهلال يخطب فقال ان اول ما نبدأبه في يومنا هذا ان نصلى ثم نرجع فتسحر (بخاری شریف، باب سنۃ العیدین لاهل الاسلام ، ص ۱۲۱، نمبر (۹۵)
The sun (must be) the measure of one or two spears until its decline. (826) And the manner of the two Eid prayers: he intends the Eid prayer, then says takbir al-tahrimah, then recites thana, then says the additional takbirs three times, raising his hands in each...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage defines the time for the Eid prayer. The author states that the valid time is from when the sun has risen to the height of one or two spears (approx. 5-10 feet) until zawal (zenith). The proofs include: (1) the hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Anbasah that the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade prayer at sunrise until it rises one or two spears, then prayer is witnessed until the sun is at zenith; (2) another hadith that prayer is permissible when the sun rises a spear's length; (3) the action of 'Abdullah ibn Busr that they finished Eid prayer at the time of tasbih (ishraq); (4) the hadith of al-Bara' that the first thing on Eid day is prayer. Thus, the Eid prayer is performed in the forenoon, after the disallowed time of sunrise, and before zawal.

Key Terms
رمح (rumh): A spear; used as a measure of the sun's height above the horizon, approximately 5–10 feet.
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith and begins to decline.
إشراق (ishraq): The time after sunrise when the sun has risen to the height of a spear; synonymous with the beginning of permissible non-obligatory prayer.
تكبيرة التحريمة (takbir al-tahrimah): The initial takbir that commences the prayer and makes what was permissible (e.g., talking) forbidden.
تكبيرات الزوائد (takbirat al-zawa'id): The extra takbirs recited after the opening takbir and thana in the Eid prayer: three takbirs in each rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does the time for Eid prayer begin?
A) At sunrise
B) When the sun is one to two spears high
C) At zawal
D) After zuhr

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer must be performed in the forenoon after sunrise (ishraq) and before the sun reaches its zenith (zawal).

Method of Eid Prayer: Procedure and Rulings
Description of the performance of Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the step-by-step method of the Eid prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify the wajibat (obligatory elements) such as the additional takbirs.

Core Idea
The Eid prayer has six additional takbirs that are wajib, not sunnah.

The Eid prayer is a special congregational prayer performed on the two Eids. Its method differs from regular prayers by the inclusion of additional takbirs (takbirat al-zawaid). The Hanafi school specifies their number and placement precisely. This lesson presents the full procedure as described in the classical texts, with attention to the conditions and obligatory elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the intention and opening takbir
The prayer begins with the intention (niyyah) for Eid prayer and the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah). Note that the intention is a condition, and the opening takbir is a rukn.
2
Recite the thana (opening supplication)
After the opening takbir, recite the thana (subhanakallahumma...). This is sunnah according to the Hanafi school.
3
Say three additional takbirs in the first rak'ah
After thana, raise your hands and say 'Allahu Akbar' three times. These are the additional takbirs (takbirat al-zawaid). They are wajib. After each takbir, let your hands rest by your sides briefly before the next one (according to some narrations).
Hanafi position: these three takbirs are after thana, before recitation.
4
Recite Quran, then perform ruku and sujud
After the three takbirs, seek refuge with Allah, recite Surah al-Fatihah followed by a surah (usually Surah al-A'la or Surah al-Ghashiyah), and then complete the first rak'ah with ruku and sujud as usual.
5
In the second rak'ah: recite Quran, then three more additional takbirs before ruku
Stand for the second rak'ah, recite Surah al-Fatihah and a surah (usually Surah al-Shams or Surah al-Ghashiyah), then say three more additional takbirs raising your hands each time. After the third takbir, say 'Allahu Akbar' for ruku to begin the bowing.
Hanafi: additional takbirs in second rak'ah are after recitation, before ruku. This differs from some other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the manner of the two (Eid prayers): he intends the Eid prayer, then says takbir al-tahrimah, then recites thana, then says the additional takbirs three times, raising his hands in each of them...
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage describes the method (kayfiyyah) of the Eid prayer. The author outlines the actions: make intention for Eid prayer, say the opening takbir (takbir al-tahrimah), recite thana (subhanakallahumma...), then say three additional takbirs (takbirat al-zawaid) raising hands each time. Then he recites Quran, then goes to ruku and sujud. In the second rak'ah, after reciting Quran, he says three more additional takbirs before bowing. Thus total additional takbirs are six. The text then again mentions the time proofs, but the core description is as stated. The proofs from companions and hadith support this number of takbirs.

Key Terms
تکبیرات زوائد (takbirat al-zawaid): The additional takbirs in Eid prayer beyond the usual takbirs.
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits actions outside prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Time and Method of Eid Prayer: Takbirs and Raising Hands
Ruling on time and takbirs of Eid prayer with prophetic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid time for Eid prayer and explain the number of additional takbirs with their evidence.

Core Idea
Eid prayer time is from sunrise to midday; six additional takbirs are proven from the Prophet's practice.

Eid prayer is a confirmed sunnah with a specific time window and unique takbirs. This lesson covers the time (from when the sun rises a spear's height until midday), the intention, the three additional takbirs in each rak'ah (total six), and the ruling of raising hands. All steps are supported by authentic hadiths, which are cited in the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time of Eid prayer
From the hadith of Abu Dawud and Nasa'i, determine that the time begins when the sun has risen a spear's height (ishraq) and lasts until midday (zawal).
The hadith of Amr ibn Abasah specifies 'not praying until it rises a spear and its rays go away'.
2
Outline the intention and opening takbir
The worshipper intends the specific Eid prayer (Fitr or Adha) and says takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir).
The text says 'yanwi salat al-'id' (intends the Eid prayer).
3
Count the additional takbirs
After reciting thana' (subhanaka), say three takbirs (takbirat zawai'id) raising the hands each time. In the second rak'ah, after recitation, say three more takbirs before bowing. Total six additional takbirs.
The Hanafi school counts three per rak'ah (total six). Other schools differ.
4
Understand the proof for raising hands
The text quotes the practice of Umar and the fatwa of Ata: raising hands with each additional takbir is established as sunnah.
Evidence from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Sunan Bayhaqi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العيدين
الشمس قدر رمح او رمحين الى زوالها (۸۲۶) وكيفية صلوتهما ان ينوى صلوة العيد ثم يكبر للتحريمة ثم يقرأ الثناء ثم يكبر تكبيرات الزوائد ثلاثا يرفع يديه في كل منها أنه قال قلت يا رسول الله ! أى الليل اسمع ؟ . .. حتى تصلى الصبح ثم اقصر حتى تطلع الشمس فترتفع قيس رمح أو رمحين فانها تطلع بين قرنی شیطان و يصلى لها الكفار ، ثم صل ما شئت فان الصلاة مشهودة مكتوبة حتى يعدل الرمح ظله ثم اقصر فان جهنم تسجر و تفتح ابوابها (ابوداود شریف، باب من رخص فیھما اذا كانت الشمس مرتفعة ، ص۱۹۱، نمبر ۱۲۷۷) (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک نیزہ بلند ہو تو نماز جائز ہے۔ سمعت عمر وبن
